Commonwealth v. Edwards


No. 773 MDA 2004


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 153; 874 A.2d 1192; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 919


January 11, 2005, Argued  
April 26, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 3, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division, No. 1832 CR 2003. Before BRATTON, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the Commonwealth argued that the evidence should not have been suppressed because defendant did not prove that he had a reasonable expectation of privacy in the residence that was searched. The appellate court concluded that the Commonwealth waived its challenge to the trial court's conclusion that defendant possessed a reasonable expectation of privacy because it did not raise the issue in the statement of questions involved or in the Pa. R. App. P. 1925 statement. The Commonwealth also argued that the parole officers had authority to enter the residence because they had reasonable suspicion that the residence contained contraband or evidence that defendant violated his parole. The appellate court concluded that entrance into the residence was illegal, and all evidence obtained after entry was subject to suppression, because when the parole officers entered the residence they did not yet have probable cause to believe that defendant resided at the residence. Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 331.27b(d)(2) could not provide them with authority to enter the residence absent consent of someone with actual or apparent authority or absent a search warrant.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

676 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Fritz v. Wright


No. 2663 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 128; 872 A.2d 851; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 857


October 26, 2004, Argued  
April 11, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Fritz v. Wright, 584 Pa. 441, 884 A.2d 250, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2216 (2005)
Reversed by Fritz v. Wright, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2026 (Pa., Oct. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Civil Division, No. 00-9454. Before MAHON, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which was entered on a jury verdict awarding appellees damages in an action for personal injuries. Appellants contended that the verdict was improperly recorded under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5104(b) because only nine jurors agreed with it.


OVERVIEW: The jury returned a verdict consisting of responses to seven interrogatories. At least 10 of the 12 jurors agreed on the answer to each interrogatory, but not the same 10 agreed on every one. While all 12 agreed that appellants' negligence was a substantial factor in bringing about appellees' harm, all 12 also found appellee was contributorily negligent. Only 10 jurors agreed that appellee's contributory negligence was not a substantial factor in bringing about the harm. Ten jurors agreed on the amount of damages; however, the identities of the two dissenting jurors were not consistent. On appeal, the court held that the "verdict," upon which five-sixths of the jurors had to agree, pursuant to § 5104(b), was comprised of all interrogatory responses, and the verdict sheet could not be parsed so as to count the votes on each question as if it were a separable verdict. Since three jurors each voted for a different result, at least in part, on the interrogatory asking whether contributory negligence was a factor and the award of damages, the court held that the verdict was the verdict of only nine of the 12 jurors, and thus, it was not a verdict at all.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for a new trial.

Commonwealth v. Thurman


No. 2289 EDA 2004


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 126; 872 A.2d 838; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 768


February 1, 2005, Argued  
April 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Thurman, 585 Pa. 688, 887 A.2d 1241, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2262 (Pa., Oct. 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, No. 08597-03. Before O'NEILL, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence reversed. Matter remanded for a new trial. Jurisidiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence entered against him by the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of various drug offenses.


OVERVIEW: During a traffic stop, the officer determined that defendant's registration had been suspended due to apparent insurance cancellation. Defendant's car was immediately impounded pursuant to a General Order of the town police department. Prior to towing, the officer conducted an inventory search and discovered illegal drugs. Defendant was convicted on drug charges. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the evidence should have been suppressed because 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6309.2 did not allow impounding and towing in the manner done in this circumstance. The court found that the statutory authority to tow a vehicle that was not properly registered contained a 24 hour grace period that allowed the owner to show that the vehicle was properly registered, which was an element that satisfied due process and prevented the Commonwealth from improperly confiscating a person's property. The court found that if given the grace period, defendant could have presented his insurance letter that showed that it was not cancelled, and the judicial authority may very well have issued a certificate of release; thus the car might not have been towed and no inventory search would have taken place.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of sentence and remanded the matter for a new trial.

 

678 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Weiner v. Fisher


No. 2563 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 118; 871 A.2d 1283; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 670


November 17, 2004, Argued  
April 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Weiner v. Fisher, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2459 (Pa., Nov. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 003585, November T, 2000. Before TERESHKO, J.



DISPOSITION: We vacate the trial court's order and remand


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and as executrix of her husband's estate, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee doctor's motion for nonsuit after the trial court ruled that the executrix's expert in a wrongful death and survival action was unqualified.


OVERVIEW: The suit alleged that the doctor was negligent in failing to follow up on the decedent's gastrointestinal symptoms and in failing to diagnose a malignancy. The trial court ruled that the executrix's expert was not qualified to testify under the provisions of the Medical Care Availability and Reduction of Error Act (MCARE), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 40, § 1303.512. The court vacated the trial court order. Contrary to the executrix's position, the trial court was correct in ruling that under § 1303. 512(b)(2), a medical expert had have been engaged in or retired from the active practice of medicine within five years of the date he gave testimony, not within five years of the date of alleged negligence. However, the trial court erred when it completely rejected the expert's teaching activities as a basis for qualification because the expert did not teach the diagnostic technique of endoscopy. The expert was offered as a gastroenterologist, which was the doctor's specialty. Thus, § 1303.512(b)(2) was satisfied if the expert was engaged in active teaching in gastroenerology. As the record could not resolve that issue, remand was necessary for reconsideration of the expert's qualifications.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings. Based on the court's ruling, it did not address the issue of whether MCARE's expert qualification requirements were unconstitutional.

Commonwealth v. Long


No. 123 WDA 2004, No. 166 WDA 2004


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 119; 871 A.2d 1262; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 496; 33 Media L. Rep. 1726


December 7, 2004, Argued  
March 31, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended April 11, 2005.
Appeal granted by, in part Commonwealth v. Long, 584 Pa. 437, 884 A.2d 248, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2072 (2005)
Appeal granted by, in part Commonwealth v. Long, 584 Pa. 438, 884 A.2d 249, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2073 (2005)
Reversed by Commonwealth v. Long, 922 A.2d 892, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1151 (Pa., May 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, No. 4201 of 1999. Before OBER, J.
Commonwealth v. Long, 572 Pa. 690, 819 A.2d 544, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 422 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenors, a publishing company and another media company, appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which denied intervenors petitions for access to the names and addresses of the jurors in a murder prosecution. The denial was based on an administrative order that required jurors to be referred to by number only.


OVERVIEW: While prospective jurors were referred to by number only, the jury selection process was open to the public and at intervenors' employees were present during voir dire. However, pursuant to Pa. R. Crim. P. 632, information on the jury questionnaires was kept confidential. Intervenors did not object to the jury selection process. It was only after voir dire that intervenors sought the jurors' names. On appeal, intervenors argued First Amendment issues. The court affirmed, holding that 1) Pa. Const. art. I, § 11 afforded intervenors no greater rights than the First Amendment; 2) while the First Amendment afforded intervenors the right of access to criminal proceedings, that right did not include a right to the names and addresses of jurors; 3) neither the administrative order's requirement for keeping jury information under seal nor the use of numbers to refer to jurors constituted a closure that triggered the Press-Enterprise requirements; and 4) as the list of empaneled jurors, which included their names and addresses, was not a "judicial document," no common law right of access to the list existed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

 

680 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gallagher


No. 1596 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 116; 874 A.2d 49; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 433


May 6, 2004, Argued  
March 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Gallagher, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 3247 (Pa., Dec. 30, 2005)
Affirmed by Commonwealth v. Gallagher, 924 A.2d 636, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1196 (Pa., June 1, 2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment of sentence reversed in part. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered after the trial court found him guilty of luring a child into a motor vehicle in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2910 and a related offense. On appeal of the luring conviction he argued that he reasonably believed the victim was at least 18 when he picked him up.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered the 17-year-old victim a ride, bought beer for them both, and eventually had sex with him. The trial court had specifically found defendant not guilty of having corrupted a minor, but nonetheless found him guilty of luring, on grounds that it was a strict liability offense. The appellate court held that luring had never been characterized as a strict liability offense, except as to the element of harming the victim, and that the appellate court had in fact held, in a previous case, that in the absence of statutory prescription of a particular level of scienter, a showing of luring had to be accompanied by a showing of knowing, intentional, or reckless conduct. That same requirement applied to the age element of the offense. The trial court, in acquitting on the corruption charge, had indicated that the victim looked older than his years, and that same mistake of fact also precluded conviction of luring.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction on the luring charge, reversed the judgment of sentence, and remanded the matter for resentencing.

Commonwealth v. Forbes


No. 3047 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 37; 867 A.2d 1268; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 113


October 5, 2004, Argued  
January 28, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence August 19, 2003. In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County. Criminal, No. 0208-0165 1/1. Before ROBINS, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), after a jury found him guilty of simple and aggravated assault, as well as burglary. He argued that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence, that the jury instruction defining burglary was erroneous, and that the "two strikes" law, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim had consensual sex, followed by an evening of acrimonious encounters, at the end of which police found the victim in his apartment, with a broken deadbolt, a television thrown to the floor, and a broken ankle. The reviewing court held that despite inconsistencies in the victim's account, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that the jury verdict, which was based on police accounts and physical evidence, was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. A jury charge challenge had been waived. Defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the two strikes law had focused on ex post facto concerns in the trial court, but on appeal he claimed that it denied him due process in the form of a trial by jury on sentencing issues. After agreeing to consider the issue because it concerned sentence legality, the reviewing court held that the Apprendi line of cases had no application, as the two strikes law established a statutory minimum, not a maximum. Moreover, it was based on the permissible criterion of criminal history. The Pennsylvania constitutional guarantee of trial by jury had already been determined not to apply to sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Bullock


No. 351 MDA 2004


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2005 PA Super 16; 868 A.2d 516; 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 16

January 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Bullock, 584 Pa. 705, 885 A.2d 40, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2083 (2005)
Affirmed by Commonwealth v. Bullock, 590 Pa. 480, 913 A.2d 207, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2520 (Pa., Dec. 27, 2006)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered upon his convictions on a jury verdict of guilty but mentally ill of third-degree murder of his girlfriend, and voluntary manslaughter in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2605 in the death of her unborn child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Pennsylvania's Crimes Against the Unborn Child Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2601 et seq., but the appellate court held that the statute clearly described what conduct was being criminalized. It further held that there was no equal protection violation because men and pregnant women were not similarly situated, and the statute rationally related to the state interest in protecting the lives of the unborn. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Smith

SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 461; 863 A.2d 1172; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4444


October 27, 2004, Submitted  
December 7, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Division, No. 6319-02. Before HAZEL, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania) following a bench trial finding him guilty of criminal attempt to commit aggravated indecent assault, sexual assault, seven counts of indecent assault, and two counts of corruption of minors. The charges involved two different victims. Defendant was sentenced to an aggregate term of incarceration of 117 months to 336 months.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence for his convictions. The appellate court found that there was sufficient evidence that defendant committed the charged attempt to commit aggravated indecent assault where testimony revealed that defendant grasped the 12 year old victim by the hair, covered her mouth, took her to the corner of a room, and put his fingers on the skin above her vagina. In addition, there was sufficient evidence that defendant committed the charged sexual assault where the evidence revealed that defendant first assaulted the 16 year old victim in December 2001 and threatened to reveal her homosexual relationship to her mother if she did not do as he said. Also, there was sufficient evidence that defendant committed the charged indecent assaults where defendant engaged in an established pattern of physical and mental intimidation of the 16 year-old victim exclusively for the purpose of sexual gratification. Finally, there was sufficient evidence that defendant committed the charged corrupting the morals of a minor where defendant consistently had inappropriate sexual contact with the two underage victims.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Kinney

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence imposed by the Juniata County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), after defendant was found guilty of two counts of accidents involving personal injury or death in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3742.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was driving, she crossed over the double yellow lines and hit an oncoming vehicle. There was sufficient evidence that defendant knew or should have known that accident involved personal injury or death. The accident took place on a clear morning on a relatively straight and flat stretch of road. The collision was severe.

Commonwealth v. Campbell


No. 279 Western District Appeal 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 440; 862 A.2d 659; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4335


January 27, 2004, Argued  
November 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Campbell, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2018 (Pa., Sept. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, No. 2803 C 2002. Before McCORMICK, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed an order of the Westmoreland County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained in a stop of a vehicle in which defendant was a passenger.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped the vehicle in which defendant was a passenger due to the driver's failure to come to a complete stop at a stop sign. The driver was unable to produce a license and registration. A second officer approached the passenger side of the vehicle and asked the passengers, including defendant, for their names and dates of birth. After obtaining this information, the second officer checked for outstanding warrants against defendant and the passenger. The second officer learned that there was an outstanding warrant for defendant's arrest. The officer asked defendant to exit the vehicle. The officer searched defendant, finding drugs on his person. As a result, defendant was arrested and charged with drug offenses. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence obtained from the search was erroneously granted. The second officer's request for defendant's name and birth date did not have to be prompted by a reasonable suspicion. Defendant did not have an expectation of privacy in his identification information. The officer's request for this information was a minimal intrusion and did not implicate Fourth Amendment or Pa. Const. art. I, § 8 protections.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The case was remanded for trial.

 

686 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Paes


No. 1213 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 430; 862 A.2d 625; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4321


June 22, 2004, Argued  
November 16, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Paes, 868 A.2d 1199, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 752 (Pa., Feb. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division, No. 1022 of 2001. Before LESKINEN, J.
Commonwealth v. Paes, 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3940 (Pa. Super. Ct., Oct. 29, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Order reversed. Judgment of sentence vacated. Jurisdiction is relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant on a charge of driving under the influence and sentenced him to nine months to five years of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped at a regulatory roadblock. He advised an officer that he was not in possession of a driver's license, his vehicle registration, or proof of insurance. He was asked to pull to the side of the road where the officer noticed signs of intoxication. Defendant failed several field sobriety tests. A blood test showed that defendant was intoxicated, which led to his arrest. His motion to suppress the evidence, based in part on the constitutionality of the roadblock, was denied. The court reversed. The state supreme court had adopted guidelines for determining the constitutionality of road blocks. The findings made by the suppression court regarding those guidelines was not supported by the record. Contrary to the suppression court's finding, there was nothing in the record that showed that the roadblock was set up based on prior administrative approval. Rather, a field officer corporal made the decision and then participated in it. Prior administrative approval was required to ensure that citizens were protected from arbitrary invasions of the unfettered discretion of officers in the field. Thus, the roadblock could not pass constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The order denying the suppression motion was reversed and defendant's judgment of sentence was vacated.

 

687 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Guilford


No. 1575 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 419; 861 A.2d 365; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3920


May 18, 2004, Submitted  
November 1, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, No. 0112-1441 1/1. Before SARMINA, J.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which imposed a life sentence under Pennsylvania's three strikes law, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714, after defendant was convicted of robbery in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3701 and possession of an instrument of crime in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 907.


OVERVIEW: When defendant was stopped and searched by police officers, the search produced a small amount of cash, a black nylon bag containing a key, and medical papers containing the name of the robbery victim. Earlier in the day, defendant, allegedly at gunpoint, took a small amount of cash and a bag from the victim. When the police apprehended defendant, the victim identified defendant. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in precluding defendant from asking the victim, at trial, whether the victim was under the influence of drugs at the preliminary hearing. Questions about the victim's drug use at a time other than the time about which the victim was testifying was not relevant to the case. The trial court erred in sentencing defendant under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714, because his prior conviction of attempted burglary involved a burglary as a second degree felony, which did not qualify as a strike for purposes of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714(g). The definition of a crime of violence under § 9714(g) corresponded with the description of first degree felony burglary under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3502(c)(1), (2) and did not include a second degree burglary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Commonwealth v. Costa


No. 2502 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 421; 861 A.2d 358; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3921


February 2, 2004, Submitted  
November 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Costa, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1609 (Pa., Aug. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division, No. 2003-2061-01. Before THOMAS, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial, the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania) convicted defendant of drug delivery resulting in death (third-degree murder) (18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2506), corruption of minors, abuse of a corpse, criminal conspiracy, and other related offenses. He appealed, alleging § 2506 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Officers discovered the body of a 16-year-old girl in a car. An autopsy revealed that she died from the adverse effects of drugs. Defendant stipulated that he provided her heroin in exchange for sex; that she took the drugs into a bathroom; that after she emerged she lost consciousness; that he tried to revive her but did not seek medical help; that he and his cousin dressed her and put heroin on her nose; and that they placed her in her car, drove it elsewhere, and abandoned it. He claimed § 2506 was unconstitutionally vague on its face because it did not specify a mens rea. The appellate court disagreed. Section 2506(a) referenced third degree murder, which was defined as any killing with malice that was not first or second degree murder. In turn, malice was defined by the common law as a defendant's conscious disregard of an unjustified and extremely high risk that his actions might cause serious bodily injury. Therefore, § 2506 sufficiently provided a mental state. Nor could defendant argue that the statute was vague as applied to his conduct, as his actions were clearly encompassed by § 2506, which applied when one delivered an illegal drug to another who died as a result.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

689 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Davidson


No. 779 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 396; 860 A.2d 575; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3835


August 16, 2004, Submitted  
October 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Commonwealth v. Davidson, 582 Pa. 356, 871 A.2d 185, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 446 (2005)
Affirmed by Pa. v. Davidson, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2451 (Pa., Nov. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Division, No. 1109-02. Before CRONIN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant raised many issues on appeal from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), after his conviction, at a bench trial, on 28 counts of sexual abuse of children by possession of child pornography, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6312(d). He challenged the weight and sufficiency of the evidence, as well as the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first argued that because the vast quantity of pornography on his computer included only 28 shots of children, his conviction was against the weight and sufficiency of the evidence. The appeals court, however, held that, taking into account defendant's considerable knowledge of computers, the trial court's finding of guilt was based on legally sufficient evidence and there was nothing shocking to the conscience about that finding. Defendant also argued that § 6312 was unconstitutionally vague, in that the definition of nudity could cover innocent behavior, and that the statute could be interpreted as prohibiting pornographic computer-generated images. The reviewing court held that nudity defined as for the purposes of sexual gratification was perfectly clear and that the trial court plainly interpreted the statute as prohibiting only pictures of real children. Finally, merger of offenses for double jeopardy purposes had no application, as each of the 28 pictures was a separate and distinct offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re M.J.M.


No. 1762 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 360; 858 A.2d 1259; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3260


May 10, 2004, Submitted  
September 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by In re M.J.M., 868 A.2d 452, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 324 (Pa., 2005)
Appeal dismissed by In re M.J.M., 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2922 (Pa., Dec. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, at No(s). 514-J-2003. Before GRIM, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which found that the juvenile had committed, beyond a reasonable doubt, acts of harassment, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2709(a)(3), and ethnic intimidation, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2710(a), and adjudicated the juvenile a delinquent.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the juvenile argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the adjudication of delinquency where the testimony established that any statements made by the juvenile were not threats or intimidation nor directed to or heard by the alleged victims. The appellate court concluded that the record contained sufficient evidence to sustain the juvenile's adjudications for harassment and ethnic intimidation where the juvenile made his remarks with the intent to harass, annoy, or alarm the victims, and the juvenile committed the harassment with malicious intention toward the victims' ethnicity. The juvenile also argued that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2710 violated his right to freedom of speech. Specifically, the juvenile argued that the statute was overbroad, void for vagueness, and/or unconstitutional as applied. The appellate court concluded that the ethnic intimidation statute was constitutional, both on its face and as applied. The juvenile was not being punished because of his opinions; rather, he was being punished because he committed harassment and the record clearly indicated that he chose his victims because of their ethnicity.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

Related proceeding at Baney v. Clerk of Court, 118 A.3d 383, 2015 Pa. LEXIS 1283 (Pa., 2015)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Baney, 2015 Pa. LEXIS 2384 (Pa., Oct. 26, 2015)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Clinton County, Criminal Division, No. 109-02. Before SAXTON, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered negotiated pleas to 30 out of 91 drug distribution charges. He appealed the negotiated aggregate sentence imposed by the Court of Common Pleas of Clinton County (Pennsylvania). Defense counsel filed an Anders brief. Defendant then filed his own pro se appellate brief.


OVERVIEW: The first issue considered by the court was whether, in light of the fact that defendant had counsel when he filed his pro se brief, the brief could be considered. Holding that the filing of an Anders brief left defendant essentially without counsel, the court ruled that consideration of the pro se brief was proper. The court then affirmed the trial court and permitted counsel to withdraw. In doing so, the court held that (1) the trial court properly dealt with all of the charges against defendant because many of the offenses, though not all, occurred in Clinton County; (2) defendant's minimum sentence was in accord with 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508 and did not violate 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9756(b); (3) the refusal to merge defendant's conspiracy and corrupt organizations convictions for sentencing purposes was proper; and (4) the trial court complied with the colloquy requirements of Pa. R. Crim. P. 590, and the record showed that defendant's entered his negotiated guilty plea knowingly and voluntarily.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed, and defense counsel was permitted to withdraw.

Commonwealth v. Dodge


No. 543 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 338; 859 A.2d 771; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2813


May 13, 2003, Argued  
August 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Dodge, 584 Pa. 672, 880 A.2d 1236, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1755 (2005)
Vacated by, Remanded by Pa. v. Timothy Mark Dodge, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2430 (Pa., Nov. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County, Criminal Division, Nos. 00CR000257, 00CR000476-00CR000492, 00CR000494, 00CR000496-00CR000500, 00CR000502-00CR000507, 00CR000510-00CR000512, 00CR000515, 00CR000555, 00CR000631, 00CR000637, 00CR000638, 00CR000785. Before MOTT, J.
Commonwealth v. Dodge, 2004 PA Super 183, 850 A.2d 1266, 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1251 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated. Case remanded. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant raised many issues on appeal from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County (Pennsylvania), challenging various evidentiary rulings and remarks by the prosecutor. He also challenged as excessive the imposition of consecutive sentences on 37 counts of receiving stolen property, resulting in an effective life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Although Pennsylvania did not have a three strikes law, the trial court's statements in connection with imposing 37 consecutive sentences, the bulk of the many offenses of which defendant was convicted, made it clear that the trial court had given up on defendant in terms of rehabilitative potential. Although defendant had waived many of the claims he hoped to have reviewed, the appellate court ruled in his favor on two of them. First, pursuant to Pa. R. Crim. P. 703, he should have received results of a psychiatric examination in sufficient time for them to be used in preparing for his sentencing. Furthermore, in the specific context of the case, the sentence was so excessive as to be unreasonable under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9781. The 37 counts were all third-degree felonies because defendant was found to have been in the business of receiving stolen property, but his crimes were not violent and much of the property had little value. Under those circumstances, imposition of a sentence that would see defendant released, at best, at aged 100, motivated as it clearly was by the trial judge's exasperation, was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions but vacated the judgment of sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing. It directed the trial court to assure that defendant received any reports in time to prepare for resentencing. It also directed the trial court to at least consider having some of defendant's sentences run concurrently.

Commonwealth v. Butler


No. 1700 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 294; 856 A.2d 131; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2333


February 24, 2004, Argued  
July 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 10, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, No. 03-01-0174 1/1. Before DYCH, J.
Commonwealth v. Butler, 2004 PA Super 253, 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2142 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of driving under the influence (DUI), carrying a firearm without a license, and carrying a firearm on public streets/public place and sentenced him to 48 hours to one year county incarceration on the DUI conviction and three years of reporting probation on the carrying a firearm without a license conviction.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the Commonwealth failed to present sufficient evidence to establish probable cause to conduct a valid stop of his vehicle. The appellate court concluded that the facts substantiated the officer's stop of defendant's vehicle on the reasonable belief that it was being operated in a careless and erratic manner at a rate of speed in excess of the posted speed limit. In addition, the evidence was more than sufficient to prove defendant was operating his vehicle while under the influence of alcohol to a degree which rendered him incapable of safe driving where the arresting officer testified that defendant "smelled like alcohol," and had bloodshot eyes, slurred speech, and an overall inability to stand up. Also, the blood alcohol test was conducted at both 3:00 a.m. and 3:45 a.m., both times within three hours after defendant drove his vehicle. The blood analysis report indicated that defendant's blood alcohol content was .106 percent and .112 percent respectively, which created prima facie evidence of intoxication under 75 Pa. Con. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(4).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Carter


No. 848 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 291; 855 A.2d 885; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2298


April 19, 2004, Submitted  
July 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Carter, 863 A.2d 1142, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3106 (Pa., Dec. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the PCRA Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, Nos. CC 9516084, CC 9600393 and CC 9604187. Before DURKIN, J.
Commonwealth v. Carter, 566 Pa. 635, 781 A.2d 138, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1537 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition brought pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 9541-9546.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised numerous issues. The appellate court concluded that the prosecutor's use of a literary allusion did not amount to prosecutorial misconduct because the allusion was in response to defendant's closing arguments wherein he attacked the various pieces of evidence in an effort to create reasonable doubt and the prosecutor was simply responding to these attempts and using oratorical flair in order to establish a theme to which the jury could relate. The suppression court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the confession for lack of the presence of an interested adult because defendant's mother refused to come to the police station. Defendant's age did not entitle him to differential treatment in sentencing. He was tried and convicted in adult/criminal court and a life sentence imposed upon an adult following a felony murder conviction did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. Defendant was not entitled to have a jury custom-tailored to suit his particular needs. He was only entitled to what he received, a jury drawn from eligible potential jurors.


OUTCOME: The order of the PCRA court dismissing defendant's petition filed pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act was affirmed.

Peters v. Sidorov


No. 694 MDA 2003, No. 695 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 292; 855 A.2d 894; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2299


April 14, 2004, Argued  
July 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 27, 2004


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Civil Division, Nos. 6346-C-2002 and 5894-C-2002. Before TOOLE, J.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two related medical malpractice actions were originally filed in Luzerne County. Appellants, two doctors and others, sought to transfer the case from Luzerne County to Montour County pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5101.1, and Pa. R. Civ. P. 1006, 2179. The Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), concluded that the cause of action arose in Columbia County and transferred venue there. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellee injured wife received outpatient medical care from the doctors in Montour County. The injured wife and appellee husband alleged that the doctors negligently prescribed a drug, which caused the wife to suffer an allergic reaction. The wife ingested the drug while in her home in Columbia County, and suffered an allergic reaction there. On appeal, appellants argued that the trial court erred in determining that a cause of action arose in the county where the injury occurred and not the county where the alleged negligence occurred. Specifically, appellants argued that venue was proper in Montour County. The appellate court concluded that it would reach an unreasonable result if it were to affirm the trial court's decision because Pa. R. Civ. P. 1006(a.1) was a very narrow venue provision in that it provided for venue in medical professional liability actions only in the county in which the cause of action arose. Since the alleged negligent acts at issue occurred in Montour County, venue was proper there.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was vacated, venue was transferred to Montour County, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Commonwealth v. Kowalski


No. 2455 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 257; 854 A.2d 545; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2147


March 15, 2004, Submitted  
July 7, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Kowalski, 871 A.2d 189, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 623 (Pa., Mar. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division, No. 2003-3025. Before RUFE, J.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which granted defendant's motion to quash the information on the count of escape, a violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5121(d)(1)(i). The charge was graded as a felony of the third degree.


OVERVIEW: When she escaped from prison, defendant was serving a sentence on misdemeanor charges. The trial court granted defendant's motion to quash on the basis that the language of § 5121(d)(1)(i) was vague and ambiguous. Alternatively, the trial court believed that § 5121(d)(1)(i) required an escape to be charged as a felony where the underlying offense was a felony, and as a misdemeanor where the underlying offense was a misdemeanor. On appeal, the court held that the escape charge was properly graded as a felony of the third degree. Pursuant to § 5121(d)(1)(i), an escape was properly graded as a felony of the third degree if it occurred following defendant's conviction of any crime for which he had been incarcerated. The court reasoned that the Pennsylvania Legislature sought to draw a distinction between detention on charges and detention after conviction for misdemeanor and summary cases.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order quashing the information and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

697 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Coleman


No. 3373 EDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 226; 854 A.2d 978; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1415


January 13, 2004, Argued  
June 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part, Vacated by, in part, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Coleman, 874 A.2d 1150, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1113 (Pa., May 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County. Criminal Division at No. 0107-1401. Before BRINKLEY, J.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), arguing that after his conviction on jury verdict of indecent assault, the trial court erred in considering the Commonwealth's motion to reconsider his sentence and in increasing that sentence after reconsideration, based on a revised assessment of his criminal history.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first argued that the trial court had not retained jurisdiction permitting it to reconsider his original sentence, but the appellate court held that the trial court had retained jurisdiction because the Commonwealth had moved for reconsideration within 10 days after imposition of the original sentence. Nonetheless, the trial court had erred in modifying the sentence. Although a military conviction could be a prior conviction for purposes of determining an appropriate sentence, because of the special restrictions on personal behavior in the military, it could not be assumed that indecent acts under military law equated to indecent assault under Pennsylvania law. In fact, the indecent acts of which defendant was convicted appeared to have been possibly consensual homosexual contacts with a fellow soldier, acts that would not have been illegal at all in Pennsylvania. Therefore, the aggravating factor of a prior conviction should not have been applied in determining defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing in accordance with the original judgment of sentence.

Commonwealth v. Moss


No. 678 WDA 2003, No. 679 WDA 2003, No. 688 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 224; 852 A.2d 374; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1408


October 20, 2003, Submitted  
June 14, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Criminal Division, at No(s). 553/02. Before MOTTO, J.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on April 4, 2003, in the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Criminal Division, at No(s). 742/02.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on April 4, 2003, in the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Criminal Division, at No(s). 498/02.
Commonwealth v. Moss, 2004 PA Super 191, 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1296 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2004)
Commonwealth v. Sullivan, 61 Pa. D. & C.4th 280, 2003 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 147 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Sentence against Moss affirmed in part and reversed in part; sentence against Austin reversed; sentence against Sullivan affirmed; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three defendants appealed from a judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania). Defendants challenged the constitutionality of the statute under which they were charged, Criminal Use of a Communications Facility, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 7512, and the sufficiency of the evidence relating to each charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' convictions were based on the use of the telephone in facilitating illegal drug transactions. Defendants' first argument was that § 7512 was unconstitutional for overbreadth and vagueness. The court disagreed. Noting that § 7512 did not include any explicit scienter requirement, the court referred to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 302(c) and stated that, construed in light of the language of § 302(c), 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 7512 was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. Defendants next argued that the stipulated evidence was insufficient to sustain their convictions. The court agreed with the trial court that there was sufficient evidence to convict two defendants, but the court concluded that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the conviction against the third defendant. As to the third defendant, the court stated that the evidence established merely that defendant engaged in drug-related telephone conversations with a known drug trafficker. Absent proof beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's conversations facilitated a specific underlying felony that was in fact carried out, the conviction could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence of one defendant, affirmed in part the sentence of another defendant, and reversed the sentence of the third defendant.

In re G.P.-R.


No. 1248 MDA 2003 , No. 1273 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 205; 851 A.2d 967; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1311


February 23, 2004, Submitted  
June 3, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, Orphan's Court and Juvenile Division, Nos. 231 1/2 of 2002 and 323 of 2001. Before HOBERG. J.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed two orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which changed the placement goal from reunification to adoption and granted the petition to terminate the father's parental rights to his son filed by the Lancaster County Children and Youth Social Service Agency.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the father raised numerous issues. The appellate court concluded that aggravated circumstances existed as to the father pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6302 for failure to maintain any substantial and meaningful contact with his son. The few letters and phone calls that the father initiated all followed the permanency hearing where the goal was initially changed to adoption. The change of goal to adoption was in the son's best interests because no bond existed between the father and the son, but the son had bonded with his foster family and was doing very well in that placement. In addition, the father received his procedural due process rights, having had the opportunity to attend various hearings, present evidence, and cross-examine the agency's witnesses. He was also represented by an attorney. Finally, the order confirming the change of goal was proper and the grant of the petition to terminate the father's parental rights was supported by the record where the trial court found that in the six-month period prior to the filing of the termination petition the father had no contact with the son and made absolutely no attempt to perform his parental duties.


OUTCOME: The orders of the trial court were affirmed.

 

700 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Ashton v. Aventis Pasteur, Inc.


No. 1969 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 202; 851 A.2d 908; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1309; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,011


December 23, 2003, Argued  
June 2, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 4026 July Term, 2002. Before COHEN, J.
Ashton v. Aventis Pasteur, Inc., 2003 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 9 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents initiated a class action suit against appellee pharmaceutical companies to secure damages for personal injuries allegedly incurred by their children as a result of an injection of a vaccine, preservative, and blood product manufactured by the companies. The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), sustained the companies' preliminary objections and dismissed the parents' complaint.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that it lacked jurisdiction because the cause of action was cognizable under the exclusive jurisdiction of the federal National Childhood Vaccine Injury Act (NCVIA), 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 300aa-1 to -34. On appeal, the parents argued that the trial court erred in concluding that it lacked jurisdiction. The appellate court found that the language of the NCVIA relative to jurisdiction was clear: a claimant's exhaustion of the NCVIA's statutory remedy was a condition precedent to subject matter jurisdiction of a state or federal court to resolve the merits of a claim filed by an individual seeking damages for a vaccine-related injury. The children were claimants and were subject to the mandate of the NCVIA requiring that an initial filing for benefits be made in the Vaccine Court. While a request for medical monitoring was a viable cause of action in Pennsylvania, the parents had to comply with the NCVIA and petition in the Vaccine Court if and when their children manifested injuries related to the ingestion of the vaccine. Thus, the parents were precluded from seeking relief in state court until they exhausted their remedies in the Vaccine Court.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

701 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. McClintic


No. 1386 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 192; 851 A.2d 214; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1303


January 13, 2004, Argued  
May 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. McClintic, 584 Pa. 155, 882 A.2d 1000, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1786 (Aug. 17, 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. McClintic, 589 Pa. 465, 909 A.2d 1241, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2272 (Nov. 22, 2006)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. McClintic, 963 A.2d 569, 2008 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3074 (Pa. Super. Ct., Sept. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, No. 02-08-0157 & 0158. Before COOPERMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered upon his conviction of robbery, burglary, and indecent assault. He challenged the sufficiency of the evidence of the third offense, as well as the application, in his case, of the three strikes sentencing statute, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence that he twice burglarized and robbed the victim, an elderly neighbor, but he argued that he should not have been convicted of indecent assault in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3126, because he pinched the victim's breast only to intimidate her. The appellate court held that nonetheless, circumstantial evidence indicated a sexual component to the touching that was sufficient to support conviction. Defendant also argued that where one of the prior strikes for purposes of his enhanced sentences was part of the same criminal episode as the third strike, he should not have been subject to the three strikes law. While the appellate court applauded the logic of defendant's argument, it was bound by the plain language of the statute, which permitted enhancement. In any event, defendant could have received the same sentences even without three strikes application. Finally, federal and Pennsylvania constitutional case law suggested, and defendant failed to effectively argue the contrary, that the statute violated neither the right to jury trial nor the right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Fausey v. Hiller


No. 1428 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 186; 851 A.2d 193; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1250


February 12, 2004, Submitted  
May 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Hiller v. Fausey, 581 Pa. 677, 863 A.2d 1147, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2546 (2004)
Affirmed by Hiller v. Fausey, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 1543 (Pa., Aug. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County, Civil Division, No. 03-20, 361. Before SMITH, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order of the Lycoming County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) granting appellee maternal grandmother partial physical custody of the minor under the Pennsylvania Grandparents' Visitation Act, 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5311 et seq.


OVERVIEW: After the child's mother died, the almost daily contact between the child and grandmother ceased due to the father's lack of cooperation. The grandmother helped to emotionally prepare the child for his mother's death. The grandmother sought partial custody and visitation rights under 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5311. Section 5311 did not violate due process. Contrary to a statute that, as applied, had been declared an unconstitutional violation of due process, § 5311 only allowed grandparents to petition for visitation or custody, a parent of the child had to be deceased, the petition could only be granted if it was in the best interest of the child, and partial custody or visitation could not interfere with the parent-child relationship. Furthermore, § 5311 placed the burden on the grandparents, not upon the parent. Section 5311 did not violate equal protection. To the extent that § 5311 treated children who had lost a parent to death differently than children who had not, it was for the justified and reasonable purpose of protecting a child's emotional well-being and accounting for the potentially different needs of a child whose parent died.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Henke


No. 357 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 178; 851 A.2d 185; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1241


January 5, 2004, Submitted  
May 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Henke, 863 A.2d 1144, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2544 (Pa., Oct. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. CC 99-10464. Before MACHEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence imposed by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of rape, involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, two counts of indecent assault, and endangering the welfare of children, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 3121, 3123, 3126, and 4304.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from various incidents of sexual acts by him with a male child victim. Defendant was sentenced to various terms of imprisonment on each count, was determined a sexually violent predator, and ordered to comply with the registration requirements of Megan's Law II, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 9791-9799.7. On appeal, defendant contended that his trial counsel was ineffective in failing to raise various constitutional challenges to Megan's Law II in that Megan's Law II violated the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. 14 and Pa. Const. art. 1, § 9. The court held that the underlying claims of the constitutionality of various provisions of Megan's Law II had previously been determined by the court and the Pennsylvania Supreme Court to lack merit. The court found that defendant's allegations were stated in a general way and that no evidentiary hearing was required to determine if his counsel was ineffective for failing to raise those claims, because failure to raise a baseless claim did not establish ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence.

 

704 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Green


No. 1962 EDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 149; 849 A.2d 1247; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 770


January 12, 2004, Submitted  
April 30, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, No. 00-01-1066. Before SHREEVES-JOHNS, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him to three to six years' incarceration followed by two years' probation under the applicable mandatory minimum statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508, for possessing a controlled substance with intent to deliver and simple possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508 was unconstitutional on its face, violating the due process, jury trial, and notice requirements of Pa. Const. art. I, §§ 6, 9. The appellate court concluded that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9712(b) and 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508(b) achieved the same end (establishing procedural requirements for imposition of mandatory minimum sentences), and used the same language regarding proof of sentencing. Thus, the caselaw upholding 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9712 against challenges identical to defendant's challenges to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508 was conclusive as to the instant case. The procedure set forth in 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9712(b) did not offend the right to trial by jury enshrined in Pa. Const. art. I, §§ 6, 9. In addition, the Commonwealth plainly notified defendant that it intended to seek a mandatory minimum sentence under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508 prior to trial, and defendant neither disputed that he received pre-trial notice nor argued how that notice was "inadequate." Consequently, defendant was not entitled to relief in any case because he lacked standing to challenge the notice requirements of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

705 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Nahavandian


No. 40 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 136; 849 A.2d 1221; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 711


January 14, 2004, Argued  
April 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part, Vacated by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Nahavandian, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 1 (Pa., Jan. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Northumberland County, Criminal Division, Nos. CR-00-214, CR-00-463, CR-00-791. Before SACAVAGE, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant raised 10 issues in his appeal from a judgment of sentence of the Northumberland County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered after his conviction of drug delivery resulting in death and various drug-related offenses. Most prominently, he challenged the consolidation of charges under two different informations as well as the constitutionality of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2506.


OVERVIEW: Survivors of a drug party in which one participant died of a heroin overdose identified defendant as having supplied the drugs. Police set up a controlled buy, obtaining a warrant to stop defendant upon his return from obtaining requested drugs, but "jumped the gun" and arrested him en route from his purchase when he deviated from his expected pattern of behavior. The appellate court held, first, that since defendant's drug dealing activity and the victim's death from an overdose each could have been admitted at a trial on the other charge, to show a common scheme, there was no error in consolidating the two informations. The statute criminalizing drug delivery resulting in death was not void for vagueness, because it incorporated a scienter requirement of general common law malice, and the evidence of defendant's guilt of that charge was sufficient. Exigent circumstances justified the police decision to stop defendant's drug run prematurely. Pretrial publicity was not so inflammatory as to mandate a venue change. Finally, the prosecutor's comments in closing fell within the reasonable limits of advocacy and did not require a grant of a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence.

Schaaf v. Kaufman


No. 2733 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 129; 850 A.2d 655; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 705


February 4, 2004, Argued  
April 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Schaaf v. Kaufman, 872 A.2d 1200, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 897 (Pa., Apr. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 3803 October Term, 1999. Before GLAZER, J.



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike granted. Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient's spouse appealed the judgment of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) finding in favor of defendant doctor in the medical malpractice case.


OVERVIEW: The patient slurred his words while reading to the spouse. The patient discussed the problem with the doctor. The doctor allegedly failed to diagnose the condition that later caused the patient to suffer a stroke. In the spouse's appellate brief, she cited a memorandum decision in support of an argument. The doctor filed a motion to strike from the brief any mention of the memorandum decision. The spouse argued that 210 Pa. Code § 65.37(A), which prohibited parties from citing the appellate court's memorandum decisions, violated the vesting clause of Pa. Const. art. V, § 1 and the due course of law clause of Pa. Const. art. I, § 11. 210 Pa. Code § 65.37(A) did not violate Pa. Const. art. V, § 1, which vested judicial power in the courts. Just because courts had been given judicial power, it did not have to exercise that power in every case. Given the appellate court's caseload, it would have been impossible for the appellate court to draft a detailed opinion for every case before it. The spouse waived her claim that 210 Pa. Code § 65.37(A) violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, as she offered no explanation in support of her argument.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted. The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Sanchez


No. 1280 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 132; 848 A.2d 977; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 708


January 26, 2004, Submitted  
April 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Sanchez, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3332 (Pa., Dec. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Criminal Division, NO. 5751 CA 2001. Before CASSIMATIS, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence imposed by the York County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) after convicting defendant of insurance fraud in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 4117(a)(3) and theft by deception in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3922(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased a vehicle for his friend. The friend was required to make the car payments. While the friend still owed money on the vehicle, she hit a tree. The car was uninsured. Defendant and the friend purchased another vehicle and obtained insurance. The damaged vehicle was added to the policy. An insurance claim was filed on the damaged car. The claim form falsified the date of the accident. Defendant signed a power of attorney form and an odometer statement in order to finalize the claim. There was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of insurance fraud in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 4117(a)(3). Defendant knew that the friend was uninsured and wanted to make an insurance claim on the damaged car. Also, defendant knew that a claim was made on the damaged car, as he prepared and signed the odometer statement and power of attorney form. There was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of theft by deception in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3922(a). Defendant obtained $ 7,731 by filing the false claim. He participated in the deception by preparing and signing the power of attorney form and odometer statement. The insurer relied upon the deception.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

In re Coats


No. 334 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 125; 849 A.2d 254; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 655


August 18, 2003, Submitted  
April 19, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County, Orphan's Division, No. 03-01-0. Before BALDWIN, J.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated; case remanded for hearing with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged the order of appellee Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County, Orphans' Court (Pennsylvania), which denied his writ of mandamus and dismissed his appeal from the orphans' court's refusal to issue him a marriage license. The prisoner's fiancee had gone to the office of the clerk of the orphans' court to obtain the license. The clerk refused the application, because the prisoner was unable to personally appear.


OVERVIEW: At a show cause hearing, the orphans' court showed that it did not have video conferencing capabilities and had insufficient staff and funds to examine the prisoner at the prison. The prison would have allowed the prisoner to have been transported and the county sheriff would have transferred the prisoner but only if he paid all expenses, which the prisoner nor his fiancee could afford to pay. The court did not question that the prisoner had a fundamental constitutional right to marry but was unable to grant his request for mandamus to compel any official to assure the prisoner's personal appearance at the clerk's office because no statutory duty existed that required such ancillary services to have been performed by such officials. The court held that there was nothing expressed or implied in the marriage license statute, 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1306, that required the clerk to visit prisons for the purpose of issuing marriage licenses and no due process or equal protection violation occurred under the facts of the case. However, the court remanded the case for the orphans' court to search for a solution to achieve the necessary face to face interview and provided suggestions.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order vacated and remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing to determine the least costly method to achieve the necessary face to face interview.

Commonwealth v. Beaman


No. 415 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 91; 846 A.2d 764; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 314


November 17, 2003, Submitted  
March 31, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Revised April 13, 2004.
Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Beaman, 580 Pa. 693, 860 A.2d 121, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2286 (Pa., 2004)
Affirmed by Commonwealth v. Beaman, 583 Pa. 636, 880 A.2d 578, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1726 (Pa., Aug. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered February 10, 2003, In the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. CC-200110942. Before MCDANIEL, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), imposed after defendant was found guilty of driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(1), (4)(i).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped at a driving under the influence roadblock. He was subsequently charged with two counts of driving under the influence. Defendant filed a motion to suppress challenging, in part, the constitutionality of such roadblocks generally. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court erred in determining that driving under the influence roadblocks were generally constitutional. Roadblocks were not per se unconstitutional pursuant to U.S. Const. amend IV. Similarly, roadblocks were not per se unconstitutional under Pa. Const. art. I, § 8. A plurality of the supreme court had upheld the constitutionality of driving under the influence roadblocks carried out in compliance with prescribed guidelines. The supreme court had applied the rationale and guidelines of the plurality decision to a subsequent case. Although defendant presented empirical data that called into question the effectiveness of driving under the influence roadblocks, the appellate court was bound by the precedent established by the highest court in the commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Pond


No. 676 MDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 81; 846 A.2d 699; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 304


December 9, 2003, Argued  
March 25, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Entered April 24, 2003, In the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, Criminal Division, No. 02 CR 732. Before CORBETT, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence reversed; jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant for violating the verification of residence provisions of Pennsylvania's Registration of Sexual Offenders Statute (Megan's Law II), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791-9799.7 (as amended May 10, 2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a sex offender who was required to report residential address changes. Failure to do so constituted a crime under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9796. Defendant attempted to do so by going to a state police barracks and providing information on a new address. The information was not correctly entered on the address change form, but defendant was not aware of that fact because he was not given a copy of the form. Defendant asserted that the Commonwealth failed to establish that he intended to violate the registration law. The Commonwealth argued that § 9796 was a strict liability law. The court disagreed, holding that (1) as the legislature had not expressed an intent that § 9796 be a strict liability law, the Commonwealth was required to establish an intent to violate § 9796; (2) the evidence did not support a finding that defendant had the requisite mens rea for violation of § 9796; (3) defendant should have been allowed to present the defense of mistake under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 304(1); and (4) defense counsel provided ineffective assistance when he acquiesced in the Commonwealth's strict liability position and failed to object to a jury instruction on the subject.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of sentence.

 

711 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Malone v. Stonerook


No. 116 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 48; 843 A.2d 1278; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 162


June 17, 2003, Argued  
February 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Malone v. Stonerook, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2132 (Pa., Sept. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order dated December 18, 2002, in the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County, Civil Division, No. 2002 GN 3205. Before MILLIRON, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff paternal grandmother against defendants, the mother and (nominally) the father, seeking partial custody of or visitation with her grandson pursuant to 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5312, the grandmother appealed from an order of the Blair County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), that sustained the mother's preliminary objections based on lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The parents' custody agreement gave the mother primary custody of their child and partial custody to the father. It also contained a provision that the grandmother was not to be left in sole charge of the child when he was with his father. The trial court had held that since the agreement amounted to a decision on the parents' part that they would discourage unsupervised contact with the grandmother, the grandmother lacked standing under § 5312. The appellate court held that the grandmother had standing under the plain language of the statute, which provided standing to any grandparent once the parents had been separated for six months. Any best interests determination would have to await an evidentiary hearing. The provision in the custody agreement was just as likely to have been inserted to prevent the father from shirking his own responsibilities and leaving the child with his mother.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the matter for an evidentiary hearing on the merits.

Cheskiewicz v. Aventis Pasteur, Inc.


No. 572 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 40; 843 A.2d 1258; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 123


June 25, 2003, Argued  
February 23, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Entered December 16, 2002, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 000952 May Term, 2002. Before DiNUBILE, J.
Cheskiewicz v. Aventis Pasteur, Inc., 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 96 (Pa. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents, on their own behalf and on behalf of their autistic child, appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), that sustained preliminary objections by defendant pharmaceutical companies to their action seeking damages for products liability and related torts, on grounds that they had failed to exhaust their federal remedies.


OVERVIEW: The National Childhood Vaccine Act, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 300aa-1 to 300aa-34, provided an administrative remedy for families of children injured by vaccines. It included a strictly applied 36-month limitations period. The parents discovered the possible link between vaccines and their child's autism after the limitations period had run, so they filed an action in a Pennsylvania court. The appellate court held that according to the plain language of 42 U.S.C.S. § 300aa-11, expiration of the limitations period did not excuse them from the requirement that they exhaust their federal remedies before proceeding in state court, even though dismissal as time-barred was virtually certain. The parents could not pursue a state court claim solely for medical expenses either, because the Act explicitly allowed recovery of such amounts. Finally, the trial court had not abused its discretion in denying an ill-conceived amendment to the parents' pleadings adding a loss of consortium claim that almost certainly would have failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order sustaining the preliminary objections.
