Commonwealth v. Dengler


No. 1314 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 38; 843 A.2d 1241; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 114


April 14, 2003, Submitted  
February 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 23, 2004.
Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Dengler, 578 Pa. 715, 854 A.2d 967, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1703 (2004)
Affirmed by Commonwealth v. Dengler, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 3208 (Pa., Dec. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, No. 2680/01. Before ESHELMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from that portion of a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), that designated him a sexually violent predator (SVP) pursuant to Pennsylvania's Megan's Law II, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 9791-9799.7. He argued that expert testimony should not have been admitted without a Frye hearing, that the evidence was insufficient, and that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's SVP hearing, the State presented evidence from a psychologist who had conducted a traditional clinical assessment of him. She testified to his long-time pattern of sexually assaulting young girls, sometimes committing an assault soon after an earlier assault. She identified him as showing mental abnormality, a sexual deviance toward young girls, that made him likely to re-offend. The appellate court held, first, that while the conclusions required under Megan's Law were new, the methods used by the expert to reach them were traditional methods of assessment, and therefore not novel in the sense of requiring a Frye hearing. Furthermore, the evidence was ample to show clearly and convincingly that defendant fit the definition of an SVP. Finally, defendant's constitutional challenges had already been rejected by Pennsylvania's highest court, so the appellate court did not consider them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence.

Commonwealth v. Bennett


No. 3511 EDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 25; 842 A.2d 953; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 70


September 4, 2003, Argued  
February 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Bennett, 582 Pa. 661, 868 A.2d 450, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 193 (2005)
Vacated by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Bennett, 593 Pa. 382, 930 A.2d 1264, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1739 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the PCRA Order of February 19, 1999, In the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, Nos. 9007-00010 2/2 & 9007-0018-0025. Before JACKSON, J.
Commonwealth v. Wyatt, 782 A.2d 1061, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3326 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appeal quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under the Pennsylvania Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 9541-46, petitioner appealed nunc pro tunc from an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), that dismissed his first PCRA petition, after the lower court had reinstated that first petition pursuant to a second petition.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court had no doubt that petitioner was entitled to a new trial on grounds identical to those on which a co-defendant had been granted one. Nonetheless, due to serial ineffectiveness of various counsel, his claim was not made on direct appeal and his first, timely, PCRA petition had been dismissed for counsel's failure to file a brief. A second petition, not timely filed within the limits of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9545, sought reinstatement of petitioner's first petition. The PCRA court allowed reinstatement, allowing petitioner to file an appeal of the dismissal of the original petition. With regret, acknowledging the clear merits of petitioner's claims and that administrative practices had been changed to prevent the recurrence of petitioner's predicament, the appellate court held that it lacked jurisdiction, given the clear directives of the Commonwealth's highest court holding that the § 9545 time limits were mandatory and jurisdictional, and that they could not be relaxed, even for equitable reasons. Therefore, petitioner's only remaining avenue was to seek review by that court by prerogative writ.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the appeal.

Commonwealth v. Manuel


No. 1785 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 21; 844 A.2d 1; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 34


October 22, 2003, Argued  
January 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Manuel, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2085 (Pa., Sept. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered October 15, 2002, Court of Common Pleas, Luzerne County, Criminal Division, No. 3918 of 2001. Before OLSZEWSKI, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a doctor, was convicted in the Court of Common Pleas, Luzerne County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), of Medicaid fraud (62 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1407(a)(6)), prescription of a controlled substance not in accordance with treatment principles (35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113(a)(14)), and two counts of prescription of a controlled substance to a drug dependent person (35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113(a)(13)). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A psychiatrist recommended that defendant be examined to determine if he suffered from dementia, but defendant refused such an exam. The trial court found that nothing in defendant's demeanor or conduct showed he was incompetent. The appellate court held that as counsel had a reasonable basis for not pursuing a competency hearing based on defendant's stated interest in protecting his medical license, defendant was unable to show that counsel was ineffective. The trial court did not assume a prosecutorial role by asking Commonwealth experts whether they had changed their opinions after being cross-examined. As two doctors testified that prescriptions defendant provided and the treatment he practiced were either inappropriate or below accepted medical standards, and a patient testified defendant provided him with drugs on request, defendant's conviction of violating Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 780-113(a)(14) was supported by sufficient evidence. The trial court properly imposed a mandatory sentence under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508(a)(2)(ii) by considering the aggregate weight of the pills defendant prescribed rather than the weight of the controlled substance in the pills.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

716 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Meals


No. 549 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 16; 842 A.2d 448; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 31


October 7, 2002, Submitted  
January 26, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Meals, 583 Pa. 661, 875 A.2d 1074, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1160 (2005)
Reversed by Commonwealth v. Meals, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2518 (Pa., Dec. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on February 28, 2002 in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Criminal Division, No. 5375 CA 2000. Before BRILLHART, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from that portion of a judgment of sentence of the York County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), that classified him, after his conviction on guilty plea to sex offenses against two young girls, as a sexually violent predator pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9794.5. He challenged the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Pennsylvania's Megan's Law, as amended, placed the burden on the Commonwealth to show by clear and convincing evidence that a person convicted of sex offenses fell within the definition of "sexually violent predator" set forth at 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9795. Case law emphasized that the mere fact of having committed a sex offense against a child did not make a person a sexually violent predator. The reviewing court noted that the Commonwealth's expert (who had not been allowed an opportunity to personally interview defendant, due to defendant's refusal to meet with him), had testified merely to the likelihood of re-offending based on statistics. Moreover, many of the determinative factors listed at 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9795.4(b) actually weighed against classification of defendant as a sexually violent offender. Under the circumstances, the evidence was simply inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in all respects except as to the sexually violent predator determination, which it reversed.

Commonwealth v. Howe


No. 1018 MDA 2002, No. 1019 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 19; 842 A.2d 436; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 32


January 6, 2003, Submitted  
January 26, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered June 6, 2002, In the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, No. 1796/01 and 1339/01. Before ESHELMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following defendant's pleas of guilty to aggravated indecent assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3125(7), and to indecent assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3126(a)(6), defendant appealed the judgments of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which found him to be a sexually violent predator and subjected him to the provisions of Megan's Law II, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 9791-9799.7.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant asserted various challenges to the constitutionality of Megan's Law II. The appellate court concluded that the registration, notification, and counseling requirements of Megan's Law II did not constitute punishment. The terms "sexually violent predator," "personality disorder," "mental abnormality," and "likely to engage in" were not impermissibly vague. Defendant did not demonstrate that he was in danger of incriminating himself of a crime during his evaluation by the State Sexual Offenders Assessment Board. The trial court did not violate defendant's right to have a "trial" initiated by indictment when he was assessed pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9795.4 because the assessment was not a "trial." Defendant's double jeopardy argument was without merit because a Megan's Law II hearing did not constitute a second trial. Megan's Law II did not violate the Pennsylvania Constitution by granting adjudicative powers to the Board because the Board dictated no specific conclusion to the judiciary. Finally, Megan's Law II did not violate Pa. Const. art. 3, § 3 because the law contained only one subject matter, i.e., the registration of sexual offenders.


OUTCOME: Defendant's judgments of sentence were affirmed.

Hollock v. Erie Ins. Exch.


No. 298 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 13; 842 A.2d 409; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 28


September 4, 2003, Argued  
January 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, Motion denied by Hollock v. Erie Ins. Exch., 893 A.2d 66, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1355 (Pa., 2005)
Appeal dismissed by Hollock v. Erie Ins. Exch., 2006 Pa. LEXIS 1544 (Pa., Aug. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment entered January 23, 2002 in the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Civil Division, No. 6790-C 1999. Before OLSZEWSKI, JR., J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of appellee insured on her claim of insurance bad faith. Both compensatory and punitive damages were awarded. The case was brought pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 8371.


OVERVIEW: The insured was injured in an accident and remained partially disabled after surgery. The insured sought recovery under the underinsured motorist (UIM) portion of her policy. The insurer denied her underinsured motorist claim, citing a lack of causation. The insurer had previously found causation and had paid the insured's claims for first-party medical benefits. The UIM issue went to arbitration where the insured was awarded an amount well in excess of the UIM coverage. Although the parties settled the UIM issue, the insured filed her bad faith action. The trial court found bad faith and made 169 findings of fact in support of its ruling. The court affirmed, holding that (1) the insurer's conduct during the course of the bad faith litigation was properly considered by the trial court in finding bad faith; (2) there was no point of law raised in the case upon which the insurer could rely to preclude a bad faith showing; (3) the evidence supported the finding of bad faith; (4) punitive damages could be awarded under § 8371 based simply on a finding of bad faith; and (5) the size of the punitive damage award was appropriate under Pennsylvania law and did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

719 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Bey


No. 1043 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 11; 841 A.2d 562; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 11


November 4, 2002, Submitted  
January 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Corrected March 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence May 16, 2001, In the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. CC200000309. Before CASHMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment designating Appellant as sexually violent predator reversed. Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled nolo contendere to one count of involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, found that he was a sexually violent predator (SVP) pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9795.4 of Megan's Law, and sentenced him to 10 to 20 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed, claiming that Megan's Law was unconstitutional and that the Commonwealth failed to prove he was an SVP.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an employee of a convalescent center, was caught in flagrante delicto with a quadriplegic patient whose brain injury had left him without cognitive function. Defendant had tested positive for HIV about six weeks earlier. Defendant had volunteered to care for the totally defenseless victim, who was in a "child-like" state, so he could act out his sexual fantasies. The trial court found that defendant was an SVP despite a Sexual Offenders Assessment Board determination to the contrary. The appellate court noted that, in determining whether a defendant was an SVP, expert testimony as to the presence of a mental defect/disorder was required. The Commonwealth produced no such proof; in fact, an assessor from the Board found that a diagnosis of defendant as having paraphilia narcissistic traits was unfounded. That the trial court gave no credence to this report did not mean the Commonwealth produced the requisite clear and convincing evidence of defendant's SVP status. Having disposed of the appeal on other grounds, the appellate court did not reach defendant's constitutional challenges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence in regard to the designation of defendant as a sexually violent predator was reversed, but was otherwise affirmed.

 

720 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lipphardt


No. 122 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 7; 841 A.2d 551; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 7


September 18, 2003, Argued  
January 12, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Indiana County, Criminal Division, No. 584 CRIM 2001. Before OLSON, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to a charge of aggravated indecent assault. The Court of Common Pleas of Indiana County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), declined to designate him as a sexually violent predator (SVP) under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9792 of the Registration of Sexual Offenders Act (Megan's Law II), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9791 et seq. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the 25-year-old victim's apartment after 2:00 a.m. and inserted his fingers into her vagina. The Commonwealth filed a praecipe to designate defendant an SVP. The State Sexual Offenders Assessment Board assessed defendant, and a Board member testified that defendant met the SVP criteria of Megan's Law II. The appellate court held that the Commonwealth could appeal the denial of SVP status, as such an appeal did not subject defendant to multiple punishments in violation of the double jeopardy clause. The trial court properly considered the factors of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. An. § 9795.4(b), and found that (1) defendant's criminal history was non-sexual in nature, except for the instant conviction; (2) defendant suffered from an anti-social personality disorder, but this disorder did not make him likely to engage in predatory sexually violent offenses; (3) defendant's sole sexual offense was not violent; (4) there was a single victim; (5) the victim was not a child, but was old enough to resist the assault. That the Board member believed defendant was likely to re-offend, and the trial court found him to be credible, was, by itself, not conclusive.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

 

721 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lipinski


No. 1101 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 3; 841 A.2d 537; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4


November 17, 2003, Submitted  
January 7, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered May 28, 2002 in the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County, Criminal Division, No. 214 Criminal 2002. Before WHERRY, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled guilty in the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County, Criminal Division, (Pennsylvania), to driving under the influence as a second offense, her sentence required the installation of an ignition interlock system before her driving privilege could be restored. She appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Certain provisions of the statutes concerning ignition interlock systems for repeat driving under the influence offenders were found to violate separation of powers and were severed from the rest of the statutes. The appellate court held the trial court had no authority to order defendant to install an ignition interlock system, as the provisions purporting to authorize such an order violated separation of powers. The legislative act providing for the installation of ignition interlock systems did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, requiring that a bill containing only one subject clearly expressed in its title. That act was entitled "An Act amending Title 42 of the Pennsylvania Consolidated Statutes, providing for the use of ignition interlock systems and for restitution of identity theft." The act's title clearly expressed its subject matter. Although the act imposed different consequences for two discrete offenses, its provisions were properly related and germane to a single general purpose, which was precise criminal sanctions. Therefore, the act did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, and the entire act did not have to be set aside.


OUTCOME: The provision of defendant's sentence imposing the installation of an ignition interlock system was vacated, but, otherwise, her conviction and sentence was affirmed.

 

722 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Anthony


No. 174 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2004 PA Super 4; 841 A.2d 542; 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3


August 12, 2002, Submitted  
January 7, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Request granted, Writ of habeas corpus denied Anthony v. Tritt, 2015 Pa. LEXIS 1918 (Pa., Aug. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence December 20, 2001, In the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County, Criminal Division, No. C.A. No. 994 - 1997. Before HANCHER, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Butler County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) convicting defendant of rape, involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, unlawful restraint, and criminal trespass, sentencing defendant to 10 to 20 years in prison, and requiring defendant to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant was subject to the registration and address verification provisions under Pennsylvania Registration of Sexual Offenders Act (Megan's Law II), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9791 et seq., defendant was not subject to the sexually violent predator provisions. Where defendant's conviction occurred prior to the effective date of Megan's Law II, the imposition of the registration and address verification requirements did not constitute an ex post facto law. The imposition of the registration and address verification requirements did not increase the penalties beyond that which was provided by statutory law, because the registration and address notification provisions did not constitute criminal punishment for constitutional purposes. The requirements, therefore, did not violate due process. While the prescribed penalties for failing to register and verify one's address under Megan's Law II were previously invalidated, those provisions were severable from the valid provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

 

723 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Antoniotti v. Eckels


No. 260 WDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 517; 840 A.2d 1013; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4613


October 30, 2003, Argued  
December 31, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division, No. 11185 of 1998. Before PRATT, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Case remanded for new trial. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff automobile passengers sought review from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which was entered against defendant two, the driver of their car, in their action against defendant one, the driver of another vehicle, arising from a collision. Defendant one had joined defendant two in the action.


OVERVIEW: The passengers, riding in a vehicle driven by defendant two, were allegedly injured when defendant one's vehicle collided with defendant two's vehicle. The passengers brought suit against defendant one, who joined defendant two and alleged that the accident was due to her negligence for, inter alia, failing to use her turn signal. Defendant two did not appear at trial and the jury returned a verdict solely against her. The passengers' post-trial relief motion was deemed denied by operation of law, and the passengers appealed, contending that the trial court erred in not allowing them to establish that defendant one was negligent for disregarding defendant two's turn signal. The court found that the trial court had erroneously interpreted Pa. R. Civ. P. 2255(c), in that it held that the admissions by default of defendant two, that her signal was not used, were binding against the passengers. As the passengers did not share identity of legal interests with defendant two, the trial court erred by binding them to her admissions. Such error resulted in substantial prejudice to the passengers, as their testimony was that the turn signal was in fact used.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for a new trial.

Commonwealth v. Kopicz


No. 580 MDA 2002, No. 581 MDA 2002, No. 582 MDA 2002, No. 583 MDA 2002, No. 584 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 499; 840 A.2d 342; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4574


October 7, 2002, Submitted  
December 19, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence March 25, 2002. In the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, No. 3621-01, No. 3622-01, No. 3623-01, No. 3624-01, No. 3625-01. Before LUDGATE, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentences affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania), which imposed sentences upon him for various sexual offenses, and which also found defendant to be a sexually violent predator who was subject to registration, notification, and counseling under the Registration of Sexual Offenders Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9791 et seq. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexually molesting five minors, and he entered open guilty pleas on a variety of charges. Based on an evaluation by the State Sexual Offenders Assessment Board, defendant was found to be a sexually violent predator who was subject to the Act. The trial court denied his post-conviction challenges to the Act and to the admission of certain psychiatric records, and he appealed. The court found that defendant's due process challenges to the Act lacked merit, in that the registration, notification, and counseling provisions were non-punitive and accordingly, the adjudication was not an "enhanced punishment." The definition of "sexually violent predator" was not unconstitutionally vague. There was no violation of the separation of powers under Pa. Const. art. 1, § 5, in that the Board did not perform an adjudicative function. The Act also was found to not violate double jeopardy, the right to privacy, or the right against self-incrimination. Lastly, denial of defendant's motion to suppress psychological reports was proper and did not violate any evidentiary privileges under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5944 and Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 50, § 7111.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of sentences of the trial court and upheld the constitutionality of the Act.

Commonwealth v. Randal


No. 523 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 465; 837 A.2d 1211; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4156


June 23, 2003, Submitted  
December 1, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended May 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence October 4, 2000. In the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. 199908779. Before O'BRIEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence imposing the installation of the ignition interlock system vacated. Judgment of sentence in all other respects affirmed. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), convicting defendant, pursuant to his guilty plea, of two counts of driving under the influence in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(1), (4), receiving stolen property in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3925, and the summary offense of windshield obstructions and wipers in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4524.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's sentence required defendant to have an approved ignition interlock device installed on all of the vehicles owned or registered in defendant's name. This requirement was imposed pursuant to Act 63, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7001 et seq. Defendant filed a petition to modify sentence, arguing that Act 63 was unconstitutional. Thereafter, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 7002(b), 7003(1), and 7003(5) were found to be unconstitutional by the supreme court, because they violated the doctrine of separation of powers. Those provisions delegated to the judiciary the executive function necessary to effectuate the issuance of an interlock restricted license. The appellate court in the instant case found that because the portions of Act 63 that required the trial court to order the installation of the ignition interlock system, verify compliance, and certify the installation to the department of transportation were found unconstitutional, the appellate court was obligated to correct the sentence imposed upon defendant. The appellate court relied upon its authority to directly amend a sentence to amend the illegal sentence imposed upon defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was vacated insofar as it imposed upon defendant the requirement that he install an ignition interlock system. The judgment of sentence was otherwise affirmed.

Rivera v. Pa. Dep't of Corr.


No. 1924 WDA 2002, No. 1925 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 447; 837 A.2d 525; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4095


September 30, 2003, Submitted  
November 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Rivera v. Pa. Dep't of Corr., 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1878 (Pa., Aug. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1924 WDA 2002: Appeal from the Order Entered October 7, 2002. In the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. Misc. 885 Oct 2000.

No. 1925 WDA 2002: Appeal from the Order Entered October 7, 2002. In the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. Misc. 886 Oct 2000. Before COLVILLE, J.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates challenged a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied their petitions for writs of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Both inmates had been previously housed in the long term segregation unit (LTSU) of the Pennsylvania prison system, and they alleged that the conditions of their confinement at the LTSU constituted cruel and unusual punishment in contravention of the Eighth Amendment. The LTSU was the most restrictive prison unit designed to house the "most problematic" inmates, and the trial court had found that, although the conditions were unpleasant, the basic requirements of life were met. The court first held that although the inmates had been transferred from the LTSU, the court would still hear the appeal because the inmates could be returned to the LTSU and other prisoners remained there; thus, the issue was capable of repetition. However, after reviewing the record of the trial court, the court concluded that the conditions complained of did not show that they either alone or in combination with other conditions, deprived the inmates of the minimal civilized measure of life's necessities, or at least a single, identifiable human need. The inmates failed to carry their burden of proving that their conditions of confinement in the LTSU were cruel and unusual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the inmates' petitions.

Commonwealth v. Haughwout


NO. 496 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 427; 837 A.2d 480; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4030


October 7, 2002, Submitted  
November 13, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgments of Sentence Entered February 26, 2001, In the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Criminal Division, Nos. 3884 of 2000; 1199 of 2001. Before MUNDY, J.
Commonwealth v. Haughwout, 2003 PA Super 26, 816 A.2d 247, 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 43 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgments of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Pennsylvania, following his guilty pleas for forgery and indecent assault, and from the trial court's determination that he was a sexually violent predator (SVP) pursuant to Pennsylvania's Megan's Law II, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 9791-99. Defendant also challenged the constitutionality of Megan's Law II.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his SVP designation. The appellate court found that the evidence clearly and convincingly supported the SVP designation. Defendant's substance abuse lowered his inhibitions and provided an opportunity for him to act out abnormal sexual urges, defendant molested his daughter a series of times, and defendant's sexual abuse of a family member increased his risk of recidivism. Megan's Law II's registration, notification, and counseling provisions did not violate defendant's right to a jury trial, as they did not impose additional criminal punishment. Further, Megan's Law II did not violate defendant's procedural due process rights in failing to provide a means for future reassessment, as given the specific legislative finding that SVPs posed a high risk of recidivism and given the lack of information concerning the prospect of successful treatment of SVPs, defendant failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality of the statute. Finally, Megan's Law II did not violate substantive due process, as defendant was not subject to confinement under the registration, notification, and counseling provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Zingarelli


No. 763 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 424; 839 A.2d 1064; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4021


September 16, 2003, Argued  
November 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Zingarelli, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1771 (Pa., Aug. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on April 5, 2002, in the Court of Common Pleas of Forest County, Criminal Division, No(s). C.D. No. 1 of 2001. Before MILLIN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Forest County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), finding defendant guilty and sentencing him for attempted statutory sexual assault and attempted involuntary deviate sexual intercourse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions. The appellate court held that defendant intended to commit a statutory sexual assault. Defendant thought that the intended victim was a 15-year-old child (actually the victim was a police officer posing as a young girl on the Internet), knew that he was more than four years older than the victim, and intended to engage in sexual intercourse per os with her. The same evidence supported the attempted involuntary deviate sexual intercourse conviction. Further, defendant intended to engage in oral intercourse with the victim, and rented a motel room, purchased wine and condoms, packed an overnight bag, and drove from Pittsburgh to Tionesta in order to meet the victim. Defendant could not invoke a renunciation defense. The appellate court refused to hold that public policy required the elimination of sting operations. The conduct of the police was not so egregious as to constitute entrapment. Finally, defendant's 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 905(b) claim was waived due to the failure to timely file a concise statement of matters complained of on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Rhoads


No. 1601 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 419; 836 A.2d 159; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4012


May 5, 2003, Submitted  
November 10, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County, Criminal Division, Nos. 2000-11684, 2000-11685. Before EBY, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which was imposed following entry of appellant's guilty plea to aggravated indecent assault, sexual assault, and indecent assault. The inmate challenged the constitutionality of the Registration of Sexual Offenders Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9791 et seq.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate's guilty plea was entered, he underwent an assessment by the Pennsylvania Sexual Offender's Assessment Board, whereupon he was declared a sexually violent predator. His sentence included imprisonment as well as the requirement that he comply with all applicable provisions of the Act for life. The appellate court upheld the constitutionality of the Act, noting that the Pennsylvania Supreme Court had upheld the Act's constitutionality as to the registration, notification, and counseling requirements, as they were not deemed to be punitive in nature. The appellate court held that appellant's constitutional challenge which hinged on the underlying assumption that those provisions of the Act constituted criminal punishment and therefore, violated due process, lacked merit. The definition of "sexually violent predator" was not unconstitutionally vague, the Act did not usurp the Pennsylvania Supreme Court's rule-making power for all courts, and it did not violate the single-subject rule of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Commonwealth v. Nguyen


No. 1669 Eastern District Appeal 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 390; 834 A.2d 1205; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3691


April 14, 2003, Submitted  
October 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Nguyen, 849 A.2d 1204, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1101 (Pa., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, No. 98-10-0677, 0678. Before DEFINO, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered upon his conviction after a bench trial of assault and related charges arising out of a shooting incident. On appeal, he challenged the constitutionality of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9712, under which he had received mandatory minimum sentences for crimes committed with a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Citing only to the Pennsylvania Constitution in his appeal, defendant argued that the mandatory sentencing statute violated the jury trial guarantee of Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 and the due process guarantee of Pa. Const. art. I, § 9. The appellate court noted, first, that federal and Pennsylvania case law had consistently held that the use of a firearm was simply a sentencing trigger, not an element of the offenses of which defendant had been convicted. Therefore, it did not have to be separately determined by a jury under the Apprendi rule. It was also already settled law in Pennsylvania that the preponderance of the evidence standard used in determining whether the trigger had been proven did not violate due process. Finally, defendant lacked standing to challenge the sentencing statute's notice provisions, since it was clear from the record that he received plenty of notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

731 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Hartner v. Home Depot USA, Inc.


No. 506 EDA 2003


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 388; 836 A.2d 924; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3690


September 10, 2003, Argued  
October 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hartner v. Home Depot USA, Inc., 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2043 (Pa., Aug. 31, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 001976 February Term, 2001. Before GODDHEART, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and matter remanded for new trial on sole issue of damages.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which, after a jury trial, entered judgment against it in the amount of $ 1 million in appellee customer's action for damages following a fall in the retailer's parking lot.


OVERVIEW: The customer, while pushing her infant in a cart, hit an unseen raised manhole cover in the retailer's parking lot. The infant sustained minor injuries and her claim was settled. The mother sustained knee injuries and underwent treatment. A jury held for the customer and the retailer filed post-trial motions, but later learned that the trial judge had retired. The newly assigned judge prepared an opinion that was considered an advisory opinion and the retailer appealed. On appeal, the court held that Pa. R. Civ. P. 227.4(1)(b) was constitutionally applied and did not deprive the retailer of the right to due process. Although the retailer's interest was important, its proposed safeguard would not have been of any value and there was a governmental interest in promoting the parties' ability to appeal. Moreover, the retailer failed to comply with Pa. R. App. P. 522. The court considered various contentions as to allegedly improper rulings by the trial court and found them lacking. However, the court held that the award of $ 1 million was against the weight of the evidence given the extent of the customer's injuries, her limited medical bills, and her failure to claim wage loss.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a new trial on the sole issue of damages. The court further relinquished jurisdiction of the case.

Commonwealth v. Lyons


No. 1210 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 360; 833 A.2d 245; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3185


April 21, 2003, Submitted  
September 22, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by, Petition denied by Commonwealth v. Lyons, 583 Pa. 695, 879 A.2d 782, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1435 (2005)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Lyons v. Beard, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 19433 (M.D. Pa., Mar. 9, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lyons v. Wilson, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 53911 (W.D. Pa., Feb. 9, 2010)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Lyons v. Wetzel, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 129891 (M.D. Pa., July 17, 2012)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Lyons v. Beard, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 178322 (M.D. Pa., Dec. 10, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, No. 852 of 2001. Before ANTHONY, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania) following his convictions related to the kidnapping, rape, and attempted murder of an eight-year-old girl. Defendant proceeded pro se with his appeal, following the denial of his post-trial motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Pennsylvania Tender Years Statute (TYS), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5985.1. The appellate court held that although the TYS was too recent to be a firmly rooted exception to the hearsay rule, it required that the evidence be proven admissible by particularized guarantees of trustworthiness. Thus, the statute was constitutional insofar as it did not violate defendant's right of confrontation under the Sixth Amendment or Pa. Const. art. I, § 9. Further, the statute was not an unconstitutional violation of defendant's right to compulsory process, as a hearing and an individualized determination of competence were required before finding a witness unavailable. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that the victim was unavailable to testify. The victim's statements to various persons were not inadmissible hearsay. Defendant was not prevented from cross-examining the nurse who took DNA samples from him. Defendant's alibi witnesses were properly excluded, as defendant failed to properly notice the witnesses. The evidence was sufficient to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

 

733 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. Allegheny Hosp.-Parkview Div.


No. 2752 EDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 349; 833 A.2d 179; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3158


March 10, 2003, Submitted  
September 18, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Dated July 25, 2002, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, at No. 2738 October Term, 1997. Before MOSS, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant health care providers appealed the order of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), finding that the health care providers were delinquent in making payment under a settlement agreement with plaintiff estate administrator and that the administrator was, therefore, entitled to a Pa. R. Civ. P. 229.1 award of sanctions.


OVERVIEW: The administrator settled her medical malpractice action that she filed against the providers. The administrator filed an affidavit under Philadelphia County, Pa., C.P. Ct. R. 229.1 for sanctions resulting from the providers' failure to deliver settlement funds. The language in the settlement and release agreement providing that each party was to bear its own counsel fees and costs did not effectuate a waiver of Philadelphia County, Pa., C.P. Ct. R. 229.1. The language in the settlement agreement dealing with counsel fees and costs clearly did not contemplate an after-the-fact enforcement proceeding. Furthermore, no waiver was effectuated, as the counsel fees and costs language did not specifically refer to Philadelphia County, Pa., C.P. Ct. R. 229.1. The trial court had authority to adopt Philadelphia County, Pa., C.P. Ct. R. 229.1, as the rule did not conflict with a statewide procedural rule or statute. Philadelphia County, Pa., C.P. Ct. R. 229.1 did not violate due process, in part, because the provision for allowing the delinquent party to file an answer to the petition for sanctions was sufficient to allow the providers an opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

734 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Connor v. Crozer Keystone Health Sys.


No. 3815 EDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 345; 832 A.2d 1112; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3153


June 10, 2003, Argued  
September 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 22, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Dated November 5, 2002. In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 000197 April Term, 2002. Before GLAZER, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix sued appellee health care providers in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), for wrongful death, and related claims. The trial court sustained the providers' preliminary objections challenging venue, and transferred venue to another county. The administratrix appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held the case was contemplated by Pa. R. Civ. P. 1006(a.1), providing that a medical professional liability action was to be brought only in the county in which the claim arose. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court's order amending Pa. R. Civ. P. 1006 to contain this provision showed it applied to actions filed on or after January 1, 2002, so it applied to the instant case. The administratrix's argument that the amendment was unconstitutional merely stated that the amendment was unconstitutional and conflicted with Pa. R. Civ. P. 152, so it was waived. The providers did not waive venue by not filing preliminary objections within 20 days, under Pa. R. Civ. P. 1026(a), or even 90 days as permitted by the order amending Pa. R. Civ. P. 1006, as the administratrix was not prejudiced. As the administratrix did not allege the providers' delay affected her ability to present factual information at trial or in opposition to their venue challenge, the preliminary objections were properly accepted. The providers did not waive venue by participating in the case pending the trial court's ruling on their venue challenges.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Long


NO. 1509 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 319; 831 A.2d 737; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2721


May 19, 2003, Submitted  
August 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Long, 841 A.2d 530, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2351 (Pa., Dec. 16, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered May 21, 2002, In the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division, No. 934 1/4 of 2001. Before LESKINEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from a judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), after he was convicted of violating the Pennsylvania Hit-and-Run Act, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3741-3755, defendant argued that he had substantially complied with the Act, that the Act violated his self-incrimination privilege, and that his sentence violated sentencing guidelines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant believed he had hit a garbage bag on the highway, but later returned and found the victim's body. He reported the accident anonymously, but did not come forward with full information about himself and the fact that he was the driver until several days later. The appellate court agreed that defendant failed to establish a defense of substantial compliance, a defense sometimes recognized in case law under the Act, since it was clear that his hesitation in turning himself in was entirely due to fear of prosecution, not to doubt about whether he had hit the victim. The appellate court went on to find that defendant's guarantees against self-incrimination under U.S. Const. amend. V and Pa. Const. art. I, § 9 had not been violated by the application of the stopping and reporting requirements of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3742 and 3744, because the requirements were a reasonable exercise of the police power to protect public safety by encouraging prompt reporting and rescue as well as financial responsibility. Finally, there was no impropriety in the trial court's having considered defendant's four-day delay, along with other factors, in determining to impose an enhanced sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Bolton


No. 2042 WDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 314; 831 A.2d 734; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2717


June 18, 2003, Argued  
August 25, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on October 21, 2002, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No(s). CL 2002-1521. Before GALLO, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of sentence by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania) finding him guilty of driving a vehicle without proper financial responsibility and driving on suspended license. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in holding that a police officer had probable cause to effectuate a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: A police officer, traveling behind defendant's vehicle, ran a National Crime Information Center (NCIC) search on the vehicle, which indicated that the vehicle, though registered, lacked the proper financial responsibility as required by 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 7886(f). Another NCIC search indicated that defendant was driving on a suspended license in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §1543(b). The appellate court held that since NCIC reports could form the basis of probable cause, the officer had sufficient probable cause to stop defendant. Therefore, the trial court properly determined that the stop was legal pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6308(b). There was no need to evaluate whether the officer was engaged in a systematic program of vehicle and driver checks. There was no need for some level of suspicion to check a license plate that was clearly in plain view.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Dellisanti


No. 1830 EDA 2001, NO. 2436 EDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 304; 831 A.2d 1159; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2433


November 7, 2002, Argued  
August 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised October 1, 2003.
Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Dellisanti, 577 Pa. 671, 842 A.2d 405, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 271 (2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Dellisanti, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1324 (Pa., June 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, No(s), 4267-00 and 7285-99. Before CORSO, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence vacated. Case remanded for resentencing. Appeal at No. 2436 EDA 2001 quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which found her guilty of violating the Corrupt Organizations Statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 911 et seq., delivery of drug paraphernalia, possession with intent to deliver drug paraphernalia, and criminal conspiracy. The Commonwealth filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: An undercover detective went into appellant's clothing store on several occasions and purchased baggies and inositol, which was used for adulterating cocaine, with the store manager's assistance. Thereafter, a search warrant was executed at the store, resulting in seizure of inositol, mannitol, and baggies. Appellant was charged and entered a plea of nolo contendre, although her motion to withdraw her guilty plea was granted. After trial, she was convicted of various charges and sentenced to various terms of probation, to be served concurrently. The appellate court quashed the Commonwealth's appeal because it was not an aggrieved party and because there was no merit to its appeal. The court held that specific intent was not a required element of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 108-113(a)(33), and that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction based on a showing of appellant's knowledge of the intended use of the paraphernalia. However, her conviction under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 911 was vacated because she was not the type of criminal, nor had she engaged in such conduct, which was the focus of that crime.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's convictions under the Corrupt Organizations Statute, vacated the judgments of sentence imposed by the trial court, and remanded the matter for resentencing. It affirmed the remaining convictions and quashed the Commonwealth's appeal.

McIntyre Square Assocs. v. Evans


No. 858 WDA 2001, No. 924 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 214; 827 A.2d 446; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1338


December 4, 2002, Argued  
May 30, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, No. GD 99-004950 and GD 99-6564. Before McFALLS, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guarantors appealed and appellee property management agent cross-appealed the judgment of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee landlord and the agent in the agent's and landlord's action to recover defaulted rent from the guarantors and issuing a non-jury verdict in favor of the landlord in the amount of $ 49,644 plus post-verdict interest.


OVERVIEW: The retail store entered into a five-year commercial lease with the landlord. The lease was executed by the property management agent acting on behalf of the landlord. The guarantors signed an agreement guaranteeing the retail store's obligations under the lease. The store executed a lease amendment in 1996 extending the lease another five years. No new guaranty agreement was signed. The store defaulted. The agent confessed judgment against the store for the default. The agent then sued the guarantors. The trial court ruled that the guaranty agreement covered the lease extension. The amendment of the lease constituted a material modification of the original lease that substantially increased the guarantors' risk. The trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the agent, as the agreement was ambiguous as to whether the guarantors agreed to guarantee material changes in the lease that increased their risk. The agent's confessed judgment was properly not given preclusive effect regarding the issue of damages against the guarantors. Because of the agent's confessed judgment, the guarantors had no right to defend the issue. Therefore, the confessed judgment was not binding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the appellate court's opinion, including an instruction to the trial court to correct the caption.

Commonwealth v. Budd


No. 1098 EDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 136; 821 A.2d 629; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 534


November 19, 2002, Submitted  
April 4, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 17, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of March 26, 2002 in the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal NO. 4259-01. Before BIEHN, J.
Commonwealth v. Budd, 56 Pa. D. & C.4th 63, 2002 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 234 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania) of institutional sexual assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a correctional officer, was arrested after he sexually assaulted a prison inmate on work release. The sexual encounter occurred when defendant, while off duty, saw the inmate going to her work-release job and offered her a ride in his car. On appeal, defendant argued that former 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3124.2 was unconstitutional. The appellate court ruled that a statute was void for vagueness only if it failed to define unlawful conduct with sufficient definiteness so that ordinary people understood what conduct was prohibited. Any person of reasonable intelligence should have known and understood the terms "inmate" and "employee or agent of the department of corrections or county correctional authority" as used in former 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3124.2. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague. No First Amendment right was implicated, so the statute was not overbroad. A statute did not violate constitutional safeguards merely because there was a doubt as to its applicability in regard to cases that may never have arisen. There was enough evidence to infer that defendant knew the victim was on work release and an inmate when he committed the sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Carter


No. 234 MDA 2002


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2003 PA Super 131; 821 A.2d 601; 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 530


September 10, 2002, Argued  
April 2, 2003, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence December 20, 2001. In the Court of Common Pleas of York County Criminal at No.: 4050 CA 2001. Before BRILLHART, J.



DISPOSITION: Remanded; Jurisdiction retained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the York County Common Pleas Court, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered after his convictions on guilty plea to charges of sex offenses against a child and other offenses, and from the trial court's reliance on a report of the Pennsylvania Sexual Offender Assessment Board in determining that he was a sexually violent predator.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an adult accused of offenses against a six-year-old girl, had been adjudicated delinquent as a juvenile for offenses involving another six-year-old girl. The appellate court held that, construed in harmony as statutes in pari materia, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9795.4 created an exception to the rules of general confidentiality of juvenile records, set forth at 42 Pa. Cons. Since the trial court had not determined which of the diagnostic and other psychiatric records considered by the Board in fact implicated disclosures made by defendant as a juvenile patient, that issue would have to be explored on remand.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter to the trial court for a further hearing to determine the extent to which materials considered by the Board included disclosures made by defendant, during his detention as a juvenile, for purposes of treatment.

Commonwealth v. Kitchen


No. 1296 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 394; 814 A.2d 209; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3816


June 4, 2002, Submitted  
December 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Commonwealth v. Kitchen, 573 Pa. 709, 827 A.2d 1201, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1262 (2003)
Affirmed by Commonwealth v. Kitchen, 576 Pa. 229, 839 A.2d 184, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2465 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered February 28, 2000, in the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County, Criminal Division, No. 99 CR 608. Before SMITH, J.
Commonwealth v. Kitchen, 797 A.2d 374, 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 564 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which imposed sentence on defendant, following his conviction of one count of sexual abuse of children by photographing sexual acts and one count of possession of child pornography. Defendant was sentenced to consecutive periods of incarceration of two to five years for each count.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6312 was unconstitutionally overbroad and that the 2 counts for which he was convicted should merge for purposes of sentencing. The appellate court concluded that there was no authority to support defendant's suggestion that an adult could take pornographic pictures of a minor, if the minor consented. 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6312 was protective in purpose, and no one could legally take pornographic photographs of a minor, regardless of whether the minor consented. Defendant's relationship with the victim was no excuse for his behavior. In addition, the issues regarding the discretionary aspects of defendant's sentence were waived, as defendant failed to include them in his Pa. R. App. P. 1925(b) statement. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the sentences should not merge, because defendant photographed the victim over 60 times in sexually explicit poses, despite the fact she was under the age of 18.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), that convicted him on 2 counts of driving under the influence of alcohol and sentenced him to 30 days' incarceration followed by 2 years' probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several issues on appeal. First, he argued that the arresting officer lacked reasonable and articulable grounds upon which to believe defendant violated the traffic control device provisions of the Motor Vehicle Code (MVC). The reviewing court found that when the officer observed defendant drive through a red light, it was established that the officer had a reasonable and articulable basis upon which to justify the stop and detention. Code § 77.24(a). Defendant also attacked the reliability of breathalyzer devices. The court held that the breathalyzer models approved for use in Pennsylvania were subjected to rigorous laboratory testing and state regulations mandating detailed calibration and accuracy procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's sentence.

Commonwealth v. Asamoah


No. 638 MDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 320; 809 A.2d 943; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2896


June 18, 2002, Argued  
October 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered March 28, 2001, in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Criminal Division, at No. 46 SCA 2001. Before DORNEY, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence reversed. Appellant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried before a district magistrate who found him guilty of violating a municipal anti-loitering ordinance. Defendant pursued an appeal, and a trial de novo was conducted. The Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania) found defendant guilty, and entered a judgment of sentence. Defendant appealed, challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance and the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed in a high drug area, holding currency in his hand. At one point, he was standing with another individual. When a police officer's vehicle approached, the two men turned and walked different directions. The other individual dropped a clear plastic zip-lock bag with an off-white substance. When defendant was subsequently observed standing on a sidewalk, still holding money in his hand, he was arrested for committing acts demonstrating an intent or desire to enter into a drug transaction. The appellate court noted that defendant was not convicted of possessing contraband substances, nor was he observed possessing any contraband substances. Rather, he was observed standing on a public sidewalk holding currency in his right hand. The off-white substance in the discarded plastic baggie was not crack cocaine. The appellate court found that the anti-loitering ordinance was vague, because it impermissibly delegated basic policy matters to police officers for resolution on an ad hoc and subjective basis. It was overbroad, by proscribing and punishing constitutionally protected activities such as "hanging around" and "sauntering." The ordinance was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was reversed. Defendant was discharged.

Commonwealth v. Gunn


No. 914 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 222; 803 A.2d 751; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1543


January 7, 2002, Submitted  
July 8, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Corrected October 3, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the PCRA Order entered April 20, 2001 in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, at No. CC 199702998. Before O'BRIEN, J.



DISPOSITION:  Order denying post conviction relief reversed. Judgment of sentence vacated. Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of robbery and criminal conspiracy, and was sentenced to 25 to 50 years' imprisonment. On direct appeal, the judgment was affirmed. Thereafter, defendant filed a petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541- 9546. The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), dismissed the petition without a hearing, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced pursuant to the provision of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714 which called for an increased penalty when a defendant had previously been convicted of two or more crimes of violence. Defendant argued that the Commonwealth failed to prove that his prior conviction for conspiracy constituted a crime of violence, and other errors. 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(g) defined aggravated assault as defined in 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2702(a)(1) or (2), or criminal conspiracy to commit any of the offenses listed. In the earlier action, defendant was charged with aggravated assault and conspiracy under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2702(a)(4). The Commonwealth added a charge of aggravated assault under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2702(a)(1). However, as part of a plea bargain the Commonwealth withdrew both counts of aggravated assault. The appellate court's review of the record did not reveal any evidence from which the sentencing court could have concluded that defendant pled guilty to conspiracy to commit aggravated assault under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2702(a)(1), or, as the sentencing court concluded, that the one count of conspiracy encompassed both underlying aggravated assault counts.


OUTCOME: The order denying postconviction relief was reversed, and the judgment of sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing.

PNC Bank v. Kerr


No. 491 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 205; 802 A.2d 634; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1220


March 19, 2002, Argued  
June 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied December 30, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 3051.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Entered on February 16, 2001. In the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, No. GD 94-4618. Before BALDWIN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee bank obtained a judgment by confession against appellant guarantor in 1994. It filed a praecipe for writ of execution on January 18, 2000; the guarantor filed a petition to open and/or stay execution on February 17, 2000. The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, denied the motion, and the guarantor appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the bank had obtained judgment by confession, the guarantor, the borrower, and the bank executed an agreement that forgave part of the debt and set out a payment schedule. When the borrower and the guarantor missed payments due, the bank sought a writ of execution. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in ruling that the guarantor's petition to open was untimely for having been filed almost six years after the confession of judgment. Because the procedures for executions upon confessed judgments extant in 1996 violated due process, new rules were adopted that year, including Pa. R. Civ. P. 2958.3, which gave the guarantor 30 days after notice of execution to file the petition to open. That rule should have been applied retroactively; further, under the First Seneca rule, as the guarantor did not "sleep on the case," but was negotiating during the six years, his petition to open was not tardy. But the guarantor's failure to assert a meritorious defense, and his unclean hands, due to sale of collateral and false financial statements, justified the trial court's denial of relief. Finally, he was not entitled to equitable accounting under Pa. R. Civ. P. 1530.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Griffin


No. 1897 EDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 203; 804 A.2d 1; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1214


May 7, 2002, Argued  
June 24, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Griffin, 868 A.2d 1198, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 342 (Pa., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Griffin v. Pa., 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5162 (U.S., June 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered October 16, 1998, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at No. 97-08-0315. Before MAIER, J.
Commonwealth v. Griffin, 760 A.2d 426, 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2736 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal (Pennsylvania), after he was found guilty of possessing a controlled substance (cocaine) and possessing a controlled substance with intent to deliver (cocaine).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court should not have imposed a term of imprisonment outside and above the ranges of the sentencing guidelines. Defendant also argued that he was entitled to have a jury determine whether he committed the prior offenses considered by the trial court when it imposed a discretionary sentencing enhancement that doubled the term of imprisonment. The appellate court concluded that defendant failed to substantiate that the trial court was unaware of the guidelines' ranges. The trial court both possessed and explicitly noted that it had considered the pre-sentence report. There was no indication that the trial court was unaware of, or ignored, any of the mitigating evidence. In addition, defendant was not entitled to have a jury determine whether he was a recidivist. Neither statutory nor case law supported the conclusion that a prior conviction for possession with intent to deliver somehow became an element of subsequent charges with that offense. The enhanced sentence was double the sentence that otherwise would have applied to the crime of possession with intent to deliver based solely on the existence of defendant's prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

Douglas v. Wright


No. 2199 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 181; 801 A.2d 586; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1168


April 15, 2002, Submitted  
June 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended August 26, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Entered December 12, 2001, In the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County, Civil Division, at No. 11057 of 2001. Before JAMES, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which granted partial custody of his three children to appellee maternal grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The father presented two issues on appeal: (1) did the trial court abuse its discretion in awarding excess custody to the grandparents greater than that which was awarded to the father at the time of his divorce and in not considering whether the visitation would interfere with the parent/child relationship, and (2) did the trial court abuse its discretion by making findings of fact and recommendations in the order which awarded elements of legal custody to the grandparents contrary to the statute. The appellate court concluded that the trial court properly conducted a detailed analysis focusing on the children's best interests when granting partial physical custody to the grandparents, and the custody order did not interfere with the father's legal custody. The record revealed a long-term, close-knit relationship between the children and the grandparents. The grandparents clearly demonstrated to the trial court that the children's best interests would be well served by granting them partial custody. The custody order was not excessive in light of the close, loving relationship the children had with the grandparents.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order granting partial custody to the grandparents.

Commonwealth v. Krouse


No. 576 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 162; 799 A.2d 835; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1022


February 19, 2002, Argued  
May 20, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Krouse, 573 Pa. 671, 821 A.2d 586, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 958 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered March 15, 2001, Court of Common Pleas of Indiana County, Criminal Division, No. 394 CRIM 2000. Before OLSON, J.



DISPOSITION: Sentence reversed in regard to the Sexually Violent Predator determination and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas, Indiana County (Pennsylvania), Criminal Division, convicted defendant of indecent assault and determined that defendant was a sexually violent predator (SVP) pursuant to Pennsylvania's Megan's Law II, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791- 9799. Defendant appealed from the judgment of sentence and the determination that he was a SVP.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's indecent assault related to oral sex in June 1999 involving a 10-year-old boy in whose house defendant was then residing. Megan's Law II was adopted effective July 2000 to correct Megan's Law I's unconstitutional process of SVP determinations. Under Megan's Law II, inter alia, a member of the assessment board had to conduct an assessment pursuant to, and include an examination of factors in, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9795.4(b). The trial court was then to hold a hearing that provided a defendant with procedural protections. The Commonwealth had to prove SVP status by clear and convincing evidence. The trial court stated the member's testimony was credible but did not detail its finding of factors. The superior court conducted plenary review of the record to conclude that there was not clear and convincing evidence of the statutory factors and a number of the statutory factors weighed against a SVP classification: the offense did not involve multiple victims, there was no evidence of force or cruelty, it was defendant's first sexual offense, and defendant's prior criminal history was non-sexual. The superior court did not have to address constitutional issues.


OUTCOME: The superior court reversed the determination that defendant was a SVP and otherwise affirmed the judgment of sentence.

Commonwealth v. Graham


No. 1352 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 159; 799 A.2d 831; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1021


March 20, 2002, Submitted  
May 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, July 5, 2001, Court of Common Pleas, Blair County, Criminal Division at No. 00 CR 943. Before CALLAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Blair County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) convicting defendant of possession of a controlled substance, possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, and criminal conspiracy to deliver a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a term of two to four years in prison. On appeal, defendant claimed that the mandatory sentencing scheme created under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6317 violated due process and constitutional guarantees of notice and jury trial. Defendant asserted that the essential element of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6317(b), delivery within 1,000 feet of school property, constituted an element of the aggravated offense. Therefore, it had to be charged in the information, submitted to the jury, and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The information did not need to allege a drug sale within 1,000 feet of a school, as it was not an essential element of the offense of possession with intent to deliver. Whether defendant violated § 6317(b) did not need to be submitted to the jury under Apprendi, because defendant received less than the statutory maximum sentence of 15 years for the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
