Commonwealth v. McCalman


No. 378 WDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 78; 795 A.2d 412; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 336


February 7, 2002, Argued  
March 20, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 30, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2278.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County, Criminal Division, No. 764 OF 2000. Before HORAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence was vacated for sole purpose of recalculation of sentence to reflect time served. In all other respects judgment of sentence was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), convicted defendant of aggravated assault, terroristic threats, recklessly endangering another person, and criminal mischief. The trial court imposed an aggregate sentence of 77 to 154 months' incarceration. Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a confrontation with his former girlfriend and her new boyfriend. During the incident, defendant pointed a gun at the boyfriend's face. Shots were subsequently fired, one of which entered the boyfriend's car, narrowly missing the former girlfriend, who was sitting in the back seat. The appellate court held the evidence was sufficient to support the aggravated assault convictions. It could be inferred that defendant, who was an expert marksman, intended to cause serious bodily injury to the former girlfriend because the bullet he fired missed her by only three inches. Testimony indicated that when the victims were running for safety, defendant continued to shoot in their direction. This conduct evidenced defendant's intent to cause them serious bodily injury. The appellate court affirmed the remainder of the convictions. However, the appellate court held defendant was entitled to 18 days' credit for time he spent under house arrest. While the case was on appeal, the state supreme court had held that a home confinement/electronic monitoring program constituted time spent in custody for purposes of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9760.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was vacated and the matter was remanded for the sole purpose of recalculating the term of the sentence, giving credit for 18 days time served. In all other respects the judgment of sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Etheredge


No. 1174 MDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2002 PA Super 58; 794 A.2d 391; 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 208


January 28, 2002, Submitted  
March 6, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Dated June 20, 2001, 1 of the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County, Criminal Division, No. 1333 of 2000. Before WALKER, J.


1 Although Appellant filed her notice of appeal from the order dated June 20, 2001, appeal is properly taken from the judgment of sentence imposed. Commonwealth v. Borrero, 692 A.2d 158 (Pa. Super. 1997); see also  Commonwealth v. Clark, 2000 PA Super 14, 746 A.2d 1128 (Pa. Super. 2000)(en banc). As the appeal was taken within 30 days following judgment of sentence, it is properly before us. We have amended the caption accordingly.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of sentence of the Franklin County Common Pleas Court, Criminal (Pennsylvania), entered upon her drunk driving conviction. She challenged the trial court's denial of her motion to suppress, as well as the constitutionality of the ignition interlock statute, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7001 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped at a police drunk driving checkpoint and subsequently charged with and convicted of drunk driving. The reviewing court that upheld her conviction first held that because the checkpoint complied with all the guidelines established by Pennsylvania's high court to assure that such checkpoints were minimally intrusive and fairly administered, the evidence gathered after defendant was stopped was properly admitted. Defendant also challenged as violative of equal protection, a claim reviewed under identical standards under Pennsylvania and federal constitutional law, the requirement at 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7003 that conditioned issuance of a restricted driver's license on her installation of an ignition interlock device into which she would have to breathe in order to start her car. Since the law did not involve suspect classifications or sensitive interests, the reviewing court applied a rational basis test, and held that the statute rationally related to the Commonwealth's interest in protecting motorists.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Baldwin


No. 526 MDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 383; 789 A.2d 728; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3533


October 29, 2001, Submitted  
December 31, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Baldwin, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2950 (Pa., Nov. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Criminal Division, No. 2087 CA 1988. Before ERB, J.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated; appellee's judgment of sentence reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty, pursuant to a plea agreement, to one count of corrupt organizations. No direct appeal was filed. Defendant's first petition, under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9541 et seq., was denied, but his second petition was granted, by order of the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which vacated his judgment of sentence. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dispositive issue, on appeal, was the timeliness of defendant's PCRA petition. Because defendant was convicted in 1989, he had until January 16, 1997 to file his petition. The appellate court found the second petition, filed on December 8, 1999, was manifestly untimely. The trial court excused the untimely filing, under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9545(b)(1)(iii), which allowed an exception for newly recognized constitutional rights. Defendant claimed there was a new case, which announced a new constitutional right. In such cases, a petition had to be filed within 60 days, under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9545(b)(2). The trial court extended the 60 days because defendant claimed he did not know about the new case in time. He presented a letter from his correctional facility, stating the new case had been received at the facility on December 22, 1999. The appellate court found that defendant's lack of awareness of the decision did not excuse the failure to file within 60 days, as neither the court system nor the correctional system was obliged to educate or update prisoners concerning case law changes. Because it was untimely, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant relief.


OUTCOME: The order granting postconviction relief was vacated and defendant's judgment of sentence was reinstated.

Commonwealth v. Crawford


No. 1958 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 373; 789 A.2d 266; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3525


August 27, 2001, Submitted  
December 27, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered September 27, 2000 in the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Criminal Division, at Nos. 1135 of 2000; 1480 of 2000. Before TOOLE, J.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in part. Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant media members appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania) denying the media members' petition to vacate or modify a restraining order precluding certain extrajudicial statements. The order also denied the media members access to the Commonwealth brief filed after defense counsel moved to quash a notice of aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: The underlying criminal matter which gave rise to the suit involved a double murder committed by two defendants, one of whom was a minor. In both instances, the Commonwealth filed a notice of aggravating circumstances, indicating its intention to seek the death penalty. The question then arose whether, because of the minor's age at the time of the murder, the death penalty was applicable. Briefs were ordered by the court for use in its deliberations on the question. At the same time, the restraining order was entered. The appellate court found that because the trial court denied not only the media members' petition to vacate or modify the restraining order, but it also denied the media members' petition to intervene, the media members were required to argue on appeal that the trial court erred in failing to grant them intervenor status. In failing to do so, they waived the issue. The media members had no alternative source of standing to challenge the restraining order, because they lacked a substantial, direct, or immediate interest in the subject matter of the litigation. The trial court properly denied access to the brief, because the brief was not a public record.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed in part, and the order was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Williams


No. 1054 EDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 355; 787 A.2d 1085; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3503


September 25, 2001, Argued  
December 14, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 28, 2002. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied June 4, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1169.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence September 10, 1996. In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County. Criminal at No. 9512-0836 1/1. Before ALLEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) convicted defendant of robbery, attempted theft, and possession of an instrument of crime, and sentenced defendant according to the Pennsylvania Mandatory Minimum Sentencing Statute (PMMSS), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9712. Defendant appealed, arguing that the sentence was illegal.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that an illegal sentence was one that exceeded the statutory limits and therefore was one which the court had no jurisdiction to impose. Because there was no dispute that defendant's sentence was within statutory limits, or that the trial court had jurisdiction to enter such sentences, defendant's challenge did not go to the legality of the sentence. Rather, it was a challenge to the discretionary aspects of sentencing. The appellate court held that to reach the merits of a discretionary sentencing issue, it was required to determine (1) whether defendant filed a timely notice of appeal, (2) whether the issue was properly preserved at sentencing or in a motion to reconsider and modify sentence, Pa. R. Crim. P. 720, (3) whether defendant's brief had a fatal defect, Pa. R. App. P. 2119(f), and (4) whether there was a substantial question that the sentence was inappropriate. The appellate court held defendant did not file a post-sentence motion challenging his sentence or object to the sentence during the sentencing hearing. Because defendant never provided the trial judge with the opportunity to reconsider or modify the sentence, the issue was waived.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Tate


No. 1775 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 348; 789 A.2d 229; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3494


October 17, 2001, Argued  
December 7, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted June 27, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1329.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence September 28, 2000 In the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County Criminal, No. 307 C.D. 2000. Before LIPSITT, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of sentence of the Dauphin County Common Pleas Court, Criminal (Pennsylvania), convicting him and sentencing him for the offense of luring a child into a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW:  18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2910 prohibited commission of conduct described as luring a child into a motor vehicle. Defendant challenged his conviction of this offense, arguing that the trial court erred in instructing the jurors that he could be found guilty if he invited a child into his car without a statutorily approved reason, even if the child never actually entered the car. For the same reason, that the child never got into the car, he challenged the sufficiency of the evidence. The appeals court upheld defendant's conviction. Prior case law construing the statute established that it was intended to constitute an inchoate offense, to prevent commission of crimes such as kidnapping, unlawful restraint, and sexual abuse of children. The words "into the car" simply described the illegal object sought by the unlawful conduct; a child did not have to enter the car for the offense to occur.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Fisher


No. 2353 PGH 1997


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 327; 787 A.2d 992; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3442


July 23, 2001, Submitted  
November 19, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence November 6, 1997. In the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County. Criminal at No. 2110 of 1997. Before DISANTIS, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence, entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), following defendant's plea of guilty to charges of rape, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3121(6), indecent assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3126(a)(7), and corruption of minors, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6301(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal the trial court erred in failing to merge the charge of corruption of minors with that of indecent assault for sentencing purposes. The appellate court noted that to be convicted of indecent assault, it must be shown an individual had indecent contact with the victim. However, the individual was guilty of corruption of minors if they performed any act that corrupted or tended to corrupt the morals of any child under the age of 18. Therefore, the appellate court advised a corruption of minors charge encompassed any such act, the consequence of which transcended any specific sex act, and was separately punishable. Accordingly, the appellate court concluded that corruption of minors was not a lesser included offense of indecent assault and the offenses did not merge for sentencing purposes. In addition, the appellate court found further analysis into the facts did not compel a different determination. The appellate court reasoned the charges of indecent assault and corruption of minors were based on separate and distinct conduct, and as such, the trial court did not err in failing to merge the convictions for sentencing purposes.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of sentence.

Commonwealth v. Atwell


No. 552 MDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 300; 785 A.2d 123; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2745


August 20, 2001, Submitted  
October 18, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered March 20, 2001, Court of Common Pleas, Adams County, Criminal Division at No. CC-706-00. Before KUHN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Court of Common Pleas, Adams County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), convicted defendant of aggravated harassment by a prisoner. At the commencement of trial, defendant moved for sequestration of two witnesses. The trial court sequestered the witnesses during their testimony but allowed the witnesses to listen to the opening statements. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the crime of aggravated harassment by a prisoner, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2703.1, was unconstitutional, and that there was no rational relationship between inmates, the class whose conduct the statute sought to control, and the legislative goal. The appellate court held that a statute whose classification did not involve a fundamental right or a suspect class did not violate the Equal Protection Clause if there was a rational relationship between the discrimination and a valid governmental matter. A rational basis analysis did not require a court to find an explanation as to why inmates and free persons were punished differently for the same offense. The deterrent effect an increased punishment could have on an inmate's conduct constituted a rational basis. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in its sequestration order. However, the appellate court found that at trial, defendant requested that each witness be absent only during the other's testimony and did not ask that the witnesses be removed during opening statements. Defendant's motion was granted as it was requested.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Dennis


No. 827 WDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 281; 784 A.2d 179; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2699


April 4, 2001, Submitted  
September 27, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 8, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 939.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered April 17, 2000, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Nos. CC 99-12286. Before O'BRIEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of rape in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, (Pennsylvania) and was sentenced. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, age 18, had consensual intercourse with the victim, age 12. Defendant believed she was 16. On appeal, defendant argued that, to the extent 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3121(a)(6) did not require the offender know the victim was under 13 and did not permit mistake of age as a defense, the statute was unconstitutional. He further claimed the imposition of a prison sentence for a crime which did not require a culpable mental state was also unconstitutional. The appellate court held that although due process considerations imposed some limitations on the absence of a knowledge requirement from a criminal offense, due process did not require that an accused be afforded the defense of mistake of the victim's age in a statutory rape case. The legislature could rationally require that one 18 years of age or older who engaged in sexual intercourse with a child below 14 years of age did so at his own peril. Although a culpable mental state was generally required before criminal sanctions could be imposed, exceptions included sex offenses, such as rape, in which the victim's actual age was determinative despite defendant's reasonable belief that the girl had reached age of consent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Gray


No. 228 MDA 2001


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 262; 784 A.2d 137; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2625



September 5, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered January 16, 2001, Court of Common Pleas, Luzerne County, Criminal Division at No. 2413 of 2000.



DISPOSITION: Judgment REVERSED. Order Denied suppression of evidence REVERSED. Case REMANDED. Jurisdiction RELINQUISHED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Luzerne County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) convicting him of several firearms and drug charges.


OVERVIEW: The officers received a tip stating that a black male wearing a red shirt was brandishing a gun. As police officers walked past defendant's apartment, they saw through the window that he was wearing a red shirt, and he had a gun sitting in front of him on a table. When the officers knocked on his door, defendant first approached the door, and he fled when he saw the police officers standing at his door. Police arrested defendant and discovered cocaine and marijuana on the kitchen table. The trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress. Although the tip was followed by defendant's retreat from the door, the facts were insufficient to establish a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. Although defendant's gun substantiated the information in the tip, the gun was not necessarily indicative of criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

In the Interest of M. D.


No. 2628 EDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 218; 781 A.2d 192; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2014


April 23, 2001, Submitted  
July 30, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order August 9, 2000, In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Juvenile Division at Nos. JUV. # 246177-09, PET. # 2541-0004. Before NEW, J.



DISPOSITION: Adjudication reversed. Case remanded for proceedings in accordance with the provisions of this opinion. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that adjudicated him a delinquent based on his conviction for possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the juvenile argued that: (1) the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress physical evidence because he matched the description broadcast over the police radio where there was no evidence introduced concerning his description, and (2) the trial court erred when it ruled that the description, coupled with his flight, provided the police with a reasonable suspicion to chase him and when it refused to suppress contraband discarded during the chase. Upon review, the appellate court reversed and remanded the judgment. The Commonwealth failed to present sufficient evidence that the officer possessed reasonable suspicion to detain the juvenile. Rather, the trial court's legal conclusion was based upon a fact not introduced into evidence. The juvenile's unprovoked flight in combination with his "partially fitting" a vague description of a robbery suspect did not give rise to reasonable suspicion, especially when the Commonwealth failed to present any evidence regarding the juvenile's proximity to the site or time of the robbery, the basis of the information supplied to the officer or any other suspicious activity on the part of the juvenile.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

764 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Edrington


No. 1651 MDA 2000, No. 1897 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 212; 780 A.2d 721; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1964


March 19, 2001, Submitted  
July 20, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Edrington, 889 A.2d 112, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4682 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence dated August 9, 2000 In the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division, No. 3974 C.D. 1999. Before HOOVER, J.
Commonwealth v. Edrington, 2001 PA Super 159, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 602 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated; case remanded for resentencing. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed, and defendant cross-appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) sentencing defendant to 10 to 20 years in prison for his aggravated assault conviction, which was his third conviction for a violent crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault, his third violent crime. Contrary to the mandatory minimum sentence, which required that a three-time violent offender be sentenced to a mandatory minimum term of 25 years under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714(a)(2), defendant was sentenced to 10 to 20 years. Although the Commonwealth failed to preserve review by filing a Pa. R. App. P. 1925(b) statement of matters complained of on appeal, the issue of a sentence's legality could not be waived. Under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714(a)(2), the trial court was required to sentence defendant to a mandatory minimum of 25 years in prison, because defendant had been convicted of three crimes of violence under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714(g). Defendant's appeal was not heard, because he did not file timely notice of appeal in accordance with Pa. R. App. P. 903(b).


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

765 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. McCandless


No. 173 EDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 168; 778 A.2d 713; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 650


January 9, 2001, Argued  
June 6, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. McCandless, 569 Pa. 507, 805 A.2d 1211, 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1448 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Entered November 10, 1999, In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County Criminal Division at No. CP# 8204-0277. Before LAZARUS, J.
McCandless v. Vaughn, 172 F.3d 255, 1999 U.S. App. LEXIS 5750 (3d Cir. Pa., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Order vacated; matter remanded for further proceedings. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At defendant's retrial for first degree murder, the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) granted defendant's motion in limine excluding the preliminary hearing testimony of an unavailable witness. State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In defendant's original trial, State was allowed to introduce the preliminary hearing testimony of a witness who was unavailable at trial. That order was affirmed. Later, on appeal of the denial of defendant's federal habeas corpus petition, the United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit ruled that defendant was entitled to a new trial as the witness was not legally unavailable, but explicitly declined to address whether there had been a full and fair opportunity to cross examine. In the interim, the witness died. At the retrial, State again tried to introduce the preliminary hearing testimony. The dead witness was unavailable, but the trial court found that defendant had not been given a full and fair opportunity to cross-examine as he did not have access to his witness statement, criminal history or his testimony agreement with State. The appellate court held that, under the law of the case doctrine, since the trial court decided against defendant on the issue of opportunity to cross examine at the first trial, it was without authority to reconsider the issue at the retrial. The trial court had reopened an issue that had already been decided and affirmed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

766 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


McCarthy v. Southeastern Pa. Trans. Auth.


No. 733 EDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 106; 772 A.2d 987; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 431


December 5, 2000, Argued  
April 10, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied November 6, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2301.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order dated January 28, 2000, Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Civil Division at No. 2855 August Term, 1996. Before FIELD, J.



DISPOSITION: Order REVERSED. Case REMANDED for a new trial. Jurisdiction RELINQUISHED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, employee, sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Philadelphia), disqualifying her chosen attorney and denying her motion for post-trial relief in an action against appellee, employer.


OVERVIEW: Employee sued employer for injuries sustained in a workplace accident. Employee's attorney obtained statements from other employees outside the presence of employer's counsel. The trial court ruled that the statements could not be used at trial, but did not directly prohibit attorney from having future communication with employer's past or present employees. Attorney subsequently contacted other employees and was disqualified for violating Pa. R. Prof. Conduct 4.2. An associate attorney tried the case and the employer was found not to be negligent. Employee was denied post-trial motions and filed an appeal. The appellate court found that the trial court's assertion that attorney was on notice that he should have no future contact with employer's past or present employees was unsupported by the record. The trial court made no finding of fact that the witnesses' statements constituted admissions for the purposes of Pa. R. Prof. Conduct 4.2. The trial court's finding regarding those employees was based on Pa. R. Evid. 803(25). Therefore, the appellate court held the trial court erred in removing attorney based on his purported violation of Pa. R. Prof. Conduct 4.2.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

767 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Wendler v. Design Decorators, Inc.


No. 743 EDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2001 PA Super 57; 768 A.2d 1172; 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 191


January 9, 2001, Argued  
February 26, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Dated January 18, 2000, In the Court of Common Pleas of PHILADELPHIA County, CIVIL at No. 3195 November Term, 1997. Before ALLEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, employer and employer's president, and dismissed all claims and cross-claims with prejudice in appellant's suit for the wrongful death of her son, an employee of appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's son was killed while working for appellee employer. Appellant sued appellees, alleging that appellees' actions were grossly negligent or negligent. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. On appeal, appellant alleged that summary judgment was improperly granted since (1) the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Act (PWCA) violated the Privilege and Immunities, Due Process, and Equal Protection Clauses, and (2) appellees recklessly/willfully disregarded federal workplace safety standards, thereby creating an exception to the exclusivity provision of the PWCA. The appellate court affirmed, concluding that the state supreme court had previously found that the exclusivity provision of the PWCA was constitutional under both the Equal Protection and Privileges and Immunities Clauses. The appellate court also concluded that appellant had failed to explain her due process claim. Finally, the appellate court reaffirmed a previous decision that the PWCA did not contain an exception for injuries caused by an employer's intentional torts.


OUTCOME: Order was affirmed. The PWCA was constitutional under both the Equal Protection and Privileges and Immunities Clauses, and it did not contain an exception for injuries caused by an employer's intentional torts.

Richards v. Hepfer


No. 496 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 394; 764 A.2d 623; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4136


September 18, 2000, Submitted  
January 26, 2001, Decided  
December 18, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised January 26, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Entered January 20, 2000, In the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County, Domestic Relations No. F.R. 1998-16733. Before WALSH, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of Court of Common Pleas, Franklin County (Pennsylvania), which awarded the paternal grandmother primary physical custody of the minor granddaughter and permitted them to relocate to Eufala, Alabama.


OVERVIEW: Since the child was 4 months-old, and living with grandmother, appellant had lived at 13 separate addresses, and father resided primarily in prison. Appellant did not regularly visit; she did not disclose where she was living, and, in an emergency, grandmother was unable to locate appellant. When the child was four, grandmother sought primary legal and physical custody. The trial court granted grandmother permission to visit Alabama, and later the trial court granted primary legal and physical custody to grandmother and permitted grandmother to relocate to Alabama, where her family lived; appellant challenged. The court affirmed. The trial court properly applied the presumption that appellant, the biological parent, had a prima facie right to custody and that grandmother had a heavy burden of production and persuasion; she carried both and the scale came down hard on her side. The trial court's findings of fact were supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; the trial court properly applied the appropriate factors in the case.

 

769 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re R.B.


No. 736 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 408; 765 A.2d 396; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4142


August 21, 2000, Submitted  
December 26, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on February 17, 2000 in the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, No. 164-J-1998. Before GRIM, J.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile who was adjudicated delinquent and placed in a treatment center following his admission to assault and terroristic threats, filed an appeal of modification of his order of disposition by the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Pennsylvania. The modification added evaluation for chemical castration in addition to his continued confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a juvenile, pleaded guilty but mentally ill to one count each of simple assault and terroristic threats. He was thereafter adjudicated delinquent and placed in a treatment facility. In the course of treatment, appellant admitted to a counselor that he had cravings to sexually assault little girls. The facility submitted a report to the court for its next periodic review hearing, which recommended that appellant undergo evaluation at a nationally recognized medical center to determine his receptivity to chemical castration. The court entered an order requiring him to remain in placement and to undergo such evaluation. Appellant filed an appeal. The court found the ordered evaluation did not conform to appellant's adjudication for assault and terroristic threats, and derived from his privileged relationship with the psychologist who uncovered the prior sexual deviance. The trial court abused its discretion in modifying its prior order of disposition, because there was not general agreement amongst experts as to the efficacy of chemical castration and the court did not receive expert testimony as to proven results for adolescents.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order for evaluation and remanded for consideration by the trial court of an appropriate treatment, noting that chemical castration for a juvenile was too radical in nature and essential to basic human behavior to be imposed by a court as a condition of probation, without statutory guidelines.

 

770 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Hickson


NO. 1920 EDA 1999, NO. 1921 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 402; 765 A.2d 372; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4223


June 6, 2000, Argued  
December 21, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted June 26, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1357.
Appeal granted by In re Hickson, 566 Pa. 664, 782 A.2d 546, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1357 (2001)
Affirmed by In re Hickson, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 655 (Pa., Apr. 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered June 17, 1999, In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division at No. 9800-9861. Appeal from the Order entered June 17, 1999, In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division at No. 9800-9866. Before SARMINA, J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought review of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), Criminal Division, decision directing the district attorney to approve appellee's private criminal complaint and file charges against parole agents, pursuant to Pa. R. Crim. P. 106, claiming appellee lacked standing to file the complaint under Rule 106 or 16 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1409.


OVERVIEW: Two parole agents shot and killed an individual while attempting to arrest him. The district attorney presented the matter to an investigating grand jury, which concluded criminal charges were unwarranted. Subsequently, appellee, a private attorney, filed a private criminal complaint against the agents. Appellee did not assert that he was appearing on behalf of the victim, related to the victim's family or acting as its representative. The district attorney refused his private criminal complaint. Appellee sued in the common pleas court, which entered judgment in appellee's favor. It directed the district attorney to approve appellee's complaint and filed charges. The Commonwealth sought review. The court reversed, finding appellee lacked standing to request a private criminal complaint. Allowing citizens, who were unconnected to an alleged crime, to file a complaint violated established legal principles wherein standing was afforded only to those who had a direct, substantial, and immediate interest in the matter to be litigated. It would have had a profoundly negative and disruptive effect on the criminal justice system.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because appellee lacked standing to file a private criminal complaint.

 

771 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Moir


No. 113 MDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 403; 766 A.2d 1253; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4224


September 18, 2000, Submitted  
December 21, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Entered October 12, 1999 in the Court of Common Pleas, Centre County, Criminal Division, at Nos. 99-684 thru 687, 99-750, and 99-925. Before KISTLER, J.



DISPOSITION: Appeal quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas, Centre County, Criminal Division, Pennsylvania, which denied his motion for reconsideration of his convictions under the Pennsylvania Game and Wildlife Code, 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 101-2965, relating to licensing violations.


OVERVIEW: Following his convictions for licensing violations under the Pennsylvania Game and Wildlife Code, 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 101-2965, appellant moved for reconsideration. Concluding that it was without jurisdiction, the court quashed the appeal. The question of timeliness of an appeal was jurisdictional. In order to preserve the right to appeal a final order of the trial court, appellant was required to file a notice of appeal within 30 days after the date of entry of that order. Appellant's motion for reconsideration did not expressly grant reconsideration within the 30 day appeal period required by Pa. R. App. P. 903(a). Indeed, the trial court did not act on the motion for reconsideration until more than 30 days after entry of the final appealable order. By that time, the trial court was without authority and lacked jurisdiction to act upon the motion for reconsideration.


OUTCOME: Appeal quashed. The court was without authority and lacked jurisdiction to act upon appellant's untimely motion for reconsideration.

Commonwealth v. Lambert


No. 1378 Harrisburg 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 396; 765 A.2d 306; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4138


September 14, 1999, Argued  
December 18, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] [EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 1 OF 2. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Post Conviction Relief Act August 24, 1998, In the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, Criminal, No. 423-1992. Before STENGEL, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of first degree murder and conspiracy, challenged an order by the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which denied her petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546.


OVERVIEW: After waiving her right to a jury trial, appellant was convicted of first degree murder, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502, and conspiracy, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903. After a death penalty hearing, appellant was sentenced to life imprisonment. The trial court denied the numerous post-trial motions but instead of filing a petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546, appellant filed a habeas corpus petition in the federal court. Over the State's objections that appellant had failed to exhaust administrative remedies, the federal district court rejected the state court's findings, and found appellant "actually innocent." The United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit reversed and while appellant's petition for certiorari with the United States Supreme Court was pending, appellant filed her PCRA petition. After a hearing, which contained almost 200 claims of after-discovered evidence, discovery violations, and ineffective assistance of counsel, the PCRA petition was denied. Following an exhaustive study of the record, the appellate court affirmed, holding that appellant had not met her burden under the PCRA statute.


OUTCOME: The denial of post conviction relief petition asserting almost 200 claims of after-discovered evidence, discovery violations, and ineffective assistance of counsel was affirmed. The period for filing such a petition was not subject to the doctrine of equitable tolling, except as provided in statute.

774 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re A.H.


No. 986 WDA 2000, No. 987 WDA 2000


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 357; 763 A.2d 873; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3408


October 18, 2000, Argued  
November 29, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, No. 241 of 1999. Before DISANTIS, J. and DUNLAVEY, J.

Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, No. 24 of 2000. Before DISANTIS, J. and DUNLAVEY, J.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County's (Pennsylvania) adjudication of her daughter and son to be dependent, issuance of a finding of aggravated circumstances as to appellant, and failure to order the Office of Children and Youth to provide reunification services for her.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother's daughter, born in March, suffered a subdural hemotoma, ostensibly committed by appellant's boyfriend in June. Six months later, while in appellant's sole care, her daughter sustained severe injuries to such an extent that she was hospitalized with multiple bone fractures. Upon hospital discharge, the daughter was put in foster care. The Office of Children and Youth (OCY) petitioned for dependency, which was granted. Aggravated circumstances were found and continued foster care placement was ordered. The same order was granted as to appellant's son after OCY, during the daughter's proceedings, discovered appellant was pregnant with him. Reunification plan with father, not with appellant, was ordered. The court affirmed as to both. Appellant admitted she was the sole caretaker at the time of her daughter's injuries and her caught-in-the-crib explanation did not match medical evidence, thus justifying the "aggravated circumstances" finding under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6302. Although appellant had unsuccessfully sought certain discovery from OCY, she had not petitioned the trial court for help. All parties had stipulated to appellant's son's dependency.


OUTCOME: Orders were affirmed. Because appellant admitted she was sole caretaker when her daughter suffered severe injuries, which did not match appellant's explanation, "aggravated circumstances" were found as to son and daughter, justifying dependency finding and denial of reunification services for appellant.

 

775 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Hutchison v. Luddy


No. 1305 Pittsburgh, 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 316; 763 A.2d 826; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3023


January 9, 1996, Argued  
October 25, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument/Reconsideration Denied January 4, 2001. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 27, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2090.
Appeal denied by Hutchinson v. Luddy, 567 Pa. 743, 788 A.2d 377, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2090 (2001)
Vacated by, Remanded by Hutchison v. Luddy, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 523 (Pa., Mar. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment Entered June 30, 1994, In the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County, Civil Division, at No. 1175 CP 1987. Before CARPENTER, J.
Hutchison by Hutchison v. Luddy, 560 Pa. 51, 742 A.2d 1052, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3501 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part as to the award of punitive damages; judgment otherwise affirmed in all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania remanded with instructions to address defendants', priest, bishop, church and diocese, request to reverse the trial court's refusal to enter a judgment n.o.v. or to award a new trial in negligence action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff minor sued to recover damages, alleging that defendant priest's conduct was part of a pattern of sexual molestation. The action also named as defendants a church, bishop, and diocese. The jury awarded $ 50,000 in punitive damages against defendant priest and $ 1,000,000 in punitive damages against other church defendants. The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania affirmed the decision of the appellate court that any liability by defendant church was barred by the statute of limitations, then remanded the cause for consideration of defendants' remaining issues. Inter alia, the appellate court held that the trial court erred in refusing to grant defendants' motion for judgment n.o.v. on the punitive damages. Although declining to recognize the tort of ministerial malpractice, the appellate court further held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in refusing to allow the defense of comparative negligence, refusing to instruct the jury regarding the doctrine of consensual agreement, and using special interrogatories that provided for the jury to find the church parties liable for either compensatory or punitive damages.


OUTCOME: Trial court's refusal to enter a judgment n.o.v. as to the award of punitive damages was reversed because the only valid cause of action, ordinary negligence, did not support the imposition of punitive damages. Judgment otherwise was affirmed in all other respects, including admission of pedophilic behavior of other diocesan priests and refusal to allow defense of comparative negligence.

 

776 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. J.H.B.


No. 1577 MDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 268; 760 A.2d 27; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2575


June 22, 2000, Argued  
September 12, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 473.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, No. 426-J-1999. Before GRIM, J.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), that placed appellee, a juvenile, under the terms of informal adjustment.


OVERVIEW: Appellee juvenile was charged by juvenile petition with simple assault and sale and use of air rifles. Informal supervision was instituted, but appellee soon ran away from home. Following appellee's later admission to the charges, and acceptance of his admission by appellant prosecution and the trial court, a hearing was conducted for disposition purposes. Appellant refused to agree to a consent decree, because a firearm was used in the offense and two victims were involved. Over objection, the trial court ordered an informal adjustment. On review, appellant sought a determination as to whether the trial court erred utilizing an informal adjustment. The court vacated the informal adjustment and remanded, because the fact that appellee ran away after informal adjustment procedures had been instituted, without petition, mandated the filing of a petition. In addition, after the petition was filed, appellant objected to a proposed consent decree, thus triggering the requirement that the matter be heard on its merits followed by findings, adjudication, and disposition.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order that placed appellee under an informal disposition and remanded, because a petition was required once appellee ran away, and once the petition was filed and appellant objected to the consent decree the statute required the matter be heard on its merits followed by findings, adjudication, and disposition.

 

777 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Wynn


No. 1111 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 271; 760 A.2d 40; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2576


May 23, 2000, Argued  
September 12, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Limited Granted May 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 917.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence March 11, 1998 entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at No. 1344 June Term, 1996. Before DEFINO, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), that entered judgment of sentence, pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714, as a high risk dangerous offender, following his conviction for aggravated assault, possession of an instrument of crime, carrying a firearm without a license, and criminal conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: After waiving his right to a jury trial, the trial court convicted appellant individual of aggravated assault, possession of an instrument of crime, carrying a firearm without a license, and criminal conspiracy. Appellee prosecution then notified appellant he was subject to sentencing pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9714(a)(1) as a high-risk dangerous offender, because aggravated assault was a crime of violence, and he had been previously convicted of a crime of violence. After a hearing, the trial court determined that appellant had failed to rebut the presumption that he was a high-risk dangerous offender. The trial court then imposed sentence. After an unsuccessful attempt, appellant sought review, challenging the constitutionality of § 9714, and arguing his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to raise the issue. The court affirmed the sentence, and in turn, found the ineffectiveness issue moot, because § 9714 did not create a presumption without requiring appellee to prove the facts that triggered the presumption, nor did it place the burden on appellant to prove he was not a dangerous offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that imposed appellant's sentence, because the statute requiring heightened punishment for high-risk dangerous offenders did not create a presumption without requiring appellee to prove facts triggering the presumption, nor did it impermissibly place the burden of persuasion on appellant. Based on that finding, the court dismissed appellant's ineffectiveness of counsel claim as moot.

 

778 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Weinberg v. Comcast Cablevision of Phila., L.P.


No. 841 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 258; 759 A.2d 395; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2467


October 5, 1999, Argued  
August 30, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 15, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 533.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment entered March 26, 1999 Docketed February 25, 1999 In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, No. 364 January Term, 1999. Before DEMBE, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant apartment owner challenged an order and judgment of the Philadelphia Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), confirming an arbitration award in favor of appellee cable provider in an action brought pursuant to the Tenants' Right to Cable Television Act, 68 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 250.501-B to 250.510-B.


OVERVIEW: After several of appellant's tenants sought cable television service from appellee, the appellee notified appellant of its intent to provide the requested service pursuant to the Tenants' Right to Cable Television Act (Act), 68 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 250.501-B to 250.510-B. The parties attempted to negotiate an agreement regarding installation; the dispute went to arbitration. The arbitrator entered an award permitting appellee to install cable service in appellant's building, ordered appellant to pay appellee $ 1 for the use of appellant's property, and ordered appellant to pay one half of the arbitration costs and to provide information about appellee's service to appellant's tenants on appellee's request. The trial court confirmed the arbitration award, and the court affirmed. The Act effected a taking, but appellant received due process beforehand. In the absence of evidence of actual damages, the nominal damages awarded were sufficient compensation for the taking. The arbitrator's award did not make appellant appellee's agent, or impose involuntary servitude upon appellant.


OUTCOME: Judgment confirming arbitration award affirmed. Arbitrator's award allowing appellee to install cable system in appellant's building was a taking of private property, but appellant received due process and just compensation.

 

779 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Black


No. 732 EDA 1999, No. 733 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 253; 758 A.2d 1253; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2114



August 25, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered January 27, 1999 In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal No. 9807-0086 1/2. Appeal from the Order entered January 27, 1999 In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal No. 9807-0086 2/2. Before YOUNGE, J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought interlocutory review of a suppression order, entered in the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), on grounds that the trial court erred in determining that defendants had a reasonable expectation of privacy in contents of a package addressed to another.


OVERVIEW: After California police intercepted a package found to contain cocaine, they tipped off Philadelphia police, who delivered it to the address indicated. Although the addressee could not be found, police observed defendants as they took the package. Later, pursuant to warrant, they found defendants with the open package and the packets of cocaine. The court held that the trial court erred in suppressing, primarily on grounds that a mailed package should have been inviolate. While defendants had an automatic right to adjudicate the merits of a suppression motion, they could not have prevailed unless they separately demonstrated an invasion of their privacy. While the addressee might have had an expectation of privacy in the package addressed to her, defendants tried to argue that they had no connection to the package, so they could not have established an invasion of privacy, or prevailed on their motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded for further proceedings. Defendants who sought to disassociate themselves from the package could not have shown the invasion of privacy required to prevail on a motion to suppress evidence.

 

780 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Fidelity Leasing, Inc. v. Limestone County Bd. of Educ.


No. 3440 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 244; 758 A.2d 1207; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2112


April 25, 2000, Argued  
August 22, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order Entered October 24, 1999 In the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Civil Division at No. 99-00570. Before CARPENTER, J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; case remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion; jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an interlocutory appeal seeking to reverse an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), Civil Division, which overruled appellant's preliminary objections to the trial court's personal jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: In an action to collect a debt, appellant debtor appealed, interlocutorily, a decision holding that appellant was subject to personal jurisdiction in Pennsylvania. The court reversed. Appellant did not have the minimum contacts necessary to subject it to personal jurisdiction. Appellant had signed a contract with appellee, a Pennsylvania corporation, agreeing to send payments to that corporation at its Pennsylvania address. Appellant also had made several follow-up telephone calls to appellee regarding the contract. However, appellant had sought to transact business with an Alabama company. That company, not appellant, initiated the contact with appellee. Appellant was not incorporated in Pennsylvania, was not authorized, licensed, or registered to conduct business in Pennsylvania, or did it have any employees in Pennsylvania. All of the negotiations involving appellant occurred in Alabama, and that is where appellant signed the contract. Such contacts were not sufficient to cause appellant to anticipate being hailed into court in Pennsylvania.


OUTCOME: Order reversed. Because appellant had not purposefully directed its activities or conducted itself in a manner indicating that it had availed itself to the forum's privileges and benefits, the trial court's exercise of personal jurisdiction over appellant was unconstitutional.

 

781 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. McMullen


No. 1600 MDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 191; 756 A.2d 58; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1551


May 24, 2000, Submitted  
July 6, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 31, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1129.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of September 9, 1999, in the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division at No. 3261/98. Before SCHMEHL, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol as a minor under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(4)(ii), in the Court of Common Pleas, Berks County (Pennsylvania), claiming the statute was unconstitutional on several grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a minor, was involved in a one-car accident. Officer noticed appellant had glassy eyes and an odor of alcohol on his breath. Appellant consented to a blood alcohol test and was determined to have a blood alcohol content (BAC) of.105. Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol as a minor. The court affirmed his conviction, finding the convicting statute was constitutional. The statute could not have been arbitrarily applied where it clearly stated minors convicted under the statute had to have a BAC of.02 or greater. Using a rational basis test, the court found the statute reasonably related to the legitimate state purpose of curbing underage drinking and driving. The legislature was allowed to set a BAC. The BAC of.02 was legitimate where it related to the variances in testing equipment and the state policy of zero tolerance.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because statute was constitutional where it was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of preventing underage drinking and driving.

 

782 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Witherspoon


No. 1784 WDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 189; 756 A.2d 677; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1524


May 17, 2000, Argued  
July 3, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied April 18, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 799. Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6589.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the ORDER October 13, 1999, in the Court of Common Pleas of ERIE County, CRIMINAL, No. 652 of 1999. Before ANTHONY, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed a decision by the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized during a search of defendant's vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession, possession with intent to deliver, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant moved to suppress evidence seized during a search of defendant's car, and the trial court granted the motion. Plaintiff State appealed the decision. The court held the trial court improperly relied on a supreme court decision for the proposition that one could never validly consent to having his car searched, subsequent to being stopped for speeding, without reasonable suspicion or probable cause. The court held the supreme court had not prohibited every search not grounded in either reasonable suspicion or probable cause. The court held defendant's consent to search the car was validly obtained. The police officer returned defendant's identification and paperwork, and informed defendant that he was free to leave. Defendant then consented to the search. The court held the search was constitutionally valid, as it flowed from a mere encounter. The court reversed the motion to suppress and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the motion to suppress, because the trial court improperly interpreted a supreme court decision as prohibiting every search not grounded in reasonable suspicion or probable cause, and defendant consented to the search of the car after being told he was free to leave.

 

783 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Adelphia Cablevision Assocs. of Radnor, L.P. v. University City Hous. Co.


No. 1209 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 184; 755 A.2d 703; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1522


February 9, 2000, Argued  
June 29, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on March 30, 1999 in the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Civil Division, No. 96-7634. Before CLOUSE, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Court of Common Pleas, Delaware County's (Pennsylvania) decision, granting summary judgment in appellee's favor, finding art. V-B of the Pennsylvania Landlord and Tenant Act, 68 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 250.501-B et seq., provided appellee access to appellant's building for the purpose of installing cable television.


OVERVIEW: Appellee provided cable television services to subscribers in the county, having been granted a franchise. Tenants of appellant property management company contacted appellee, requesting service. Pursuant to art. V-B of the Pennsylvania Landlord and Tenant Act, 68 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 250.501-B et seq., appellee requested access to apartment complexes for the purpose of installing services. Appellant failed to grant access, requesting appellee address certain installation issues. Appellee sought a declaratory judgment, claiming entitlement to obtain information needed to prepare an installation proposal. The court affirmed summary judgment for appellee. Appellee's requests were in the public interest and justified grants of eminent domain power to cable operators. The statute met due process requirements where notice and opportunity to be heard were required and the arbitrator's decision could have been appealed. Compensation to landlord for loss to property value was required, meeting constitutional requirements of just compensation for takings.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the statute provided appellee access to appellant's building for the purpose of installing cable television where the statute met due process and takings requirements.

 

784 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of J.Y.


NO. 1363 WDA 1999, No. 1777 WDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 169; 754 A.2d 5; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1076


March 29, 2000, Submitted  
June 7, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied December 19, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered July 14, 1999 In the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Civil No. 111 WCCB 1997. Before MARKER, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and father, filed an appeal of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania) that implemented a change of goal from reunification to adoption regarding two minor children.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, mother and father, had their two minor children removed from their care follow a declaration that the children were dependent. The trial court conducted three permanency review hearings, and at the third one, it was found appellants had made minimal progress toward alleviating the circumstances which necessitated placement and that the minor children were doing exceedingly well in their foster placement. Appellants filed an appeal. Affirming the trial court's determination, the court held nothing prevented the trial court from taking appellants' refusal to comply the mental health program into account when determining whether to change the goal for the minor children. Rather it was appellants' failure to attend GED classes or participate in drug and alcohol treatment, as well as the criminal charges facing both of them, that was the basis for the trial court's change of goal. Further, appellant mother was not entitled to suppression of evidence regarding her sexual relations with a 13 year old girl because dependency proceedings did not provide for suppression hearings.


OUTCOME: Trial court's change of goal that minor children should be adopted rather than reunited with appellants, mother and father, affirmed; appellants' failure to attend GED classes or participate in drug and alcohol treatment, as well as the criminal charges facing both of them, was the basis for the trial court's change of goal.

 

785 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Hennigan


No. 3325 Philadelphia 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 145; 753 A.2d 245; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 662


August 9, 1999, Submitted  
May 9, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from JUDGMENT OF SENTENCE October 8, 1998, in the Court of Common Pleas of PHILADELPHIA County, CRIMINAL, No. 98-03-0911 2/2. Before MAIER, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed for possession with intent to deliver and for criminal conspiracy. Judgment of sentence vacated for firearms not to be carried without a license. Case remanded for resentencing. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, criminal conspiracy, and firearms not to be carried without a license, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) contending the inventory search of his vehicle was improper.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, criminal conspiracy, and firearms not to be carried without a license. Appellant was legally responsible as an accomplice for the underlying crime of possession with intent to deliver. The search of appellant's car parked legally on the street was not within the caretaking function of the police, thus it was not properly conducted without a warrant. Appellant's vehicle was not shown to cause a public safety or traffic control concern. The court held the commonwealth failed to demonstrate the police had the statutory authority under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3352(c)(3) to impound appellant's vehicle. Because the record failed to demonstrate a community care-taking function was served by impoundment, the police did not obtain lawful custody of the vehicle when the police impounded it and the trial court erred when it denied the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Conviction for firearms not to be carried without a license vacated and remanded for sentencing. Other convictions affirmed. The commonwealth did not demonstrate its authority to impound vehicle, thus inventory search improper, and trial court erred by refusing to grant motion to suppress.

 

786 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Murray


No. 195 Pittsburgh 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 84; 749 A.2d 513; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 294


September 8, 1999, Argued  
March 21, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered December 30, 1997, in the Court of Common Pleas of Venango County, Criminal CR No. 476 of 1997. Before WHITE, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Venango County (Pennsylvania); a divided panel of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania held Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a.1) unconstitutional, and the issue was then reargued before the Superior Court of Pennsylvania en banc.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(4). Appellant's blood alcohol content (BAC), tested approximately 30 minutes after appellant was pulled over by a police officer, was above the limit set forth in 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(4). The trial court instructed the jury that it was permitted to infer that appellant's BAC was above the limit while he was driving, pursuant to 75 Pa Cons. Stat. § 3731(a.1). 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a.1) was constitutional as it did not impose absolute liability but created a common sense permissive evidentiary inference based upon the BAC, so long as the testing occurred within three hours of driving. The jury was not required to conclude that appellant's BAC was over the limit. The evidence presented was legally sufficient to sustain appellant's conviction under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(4).


OUTCOME: Judgment of sentence affirmed; the statute under which appellant was convicted was constitutional, the jury instruction was consistent with the proper use of inference, and the evidence presented was legally sufficient to sustain the conviction.

 

787 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


DOT v. Taylor


No. 1016 Pittsburgh 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 27; 746 A.2d 626; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 75


December 1, 1999, Argued  
February 1, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted September 26, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2349.
Appeal granted by DOT v. Taylor, 565 Pa. 644, 771 A.2d 1284, 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2349 (2000)
Later proceeding at Commonwealth v. Taylor, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 457 (Pa., Mar. 7, 2001)
Reversed by DOT v. Taylor, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 25 (Pa., Jan. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered March 9, 1998, Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County, Criminal Division at No. CC 9610950. Before ZOTTOLA, J.
DOT v. Taylor, 1999 PA Super 174, 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1894 (Pa. Super. Ct., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Order AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Transportation appealed the order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), affirming the trial court's denial of appellant's motion to quash appellee's subpoena and ordering appellant to produce accident investigations and safety studies of the road on which appellee's automobile accident occurred.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was prosecuted for vehicular homicide and driving under the influence. Appellee sought production of documents pertaining to appellant's accident investigations and safety studies of the road on which the accident occurred. The trial court ordered appellant to produce the documents. Appellant argued the materials were privileged under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3754(b). The court held that appellee's request fell outside the scope of the limited privilege of § 3754. The purpose of the section, providing appellant unbiased information regarding accidents, was not adversely impacted by the disclosure. The information subject to production was specified in detail by the trial court, and was limited to one specific date and specific numbered segments of a specific state road. The order restricted the persons to whom the information would be made available and stated that it could only be used for the preparation and presentation of appellee's defense.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed because the disclosure fell outside the scope of the limited privilege of the statute since it did not adversely impact the statute's purpose, the information subject to disclosure was specifically identified, and to whom the information could be given and for what it could be used was limited.

 

788 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Zugay


No. 242 MDA 99


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2000 PA Super 15; 745 A.2d 639; 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 14


November 8, 1999, Submitted  
January 19, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 11, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of December 17, 1998 in the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, Criminal No. 213 of 98. Before QUIGLEY, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Perry County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(1), (a)(4).


OVERVIEW: After wrecking his truck, police questioned appellant, noting his eyes were bloodshot, he smelled of alcohol, and his speech was slurred. Appellant was arrested, blood was drawn, and his blood-alcohol content (BAC) was over 0.10 percent. Convicted of driving while under the influence of alcohol (DUI), appellant appealed, challenging the admissibility, weight and credibility of the evidence. The court affirmed. Evidence of appellant's BAC was admissible under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547(c) and (d)(3) to prove appellant violated 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(1) and (a)(4). Appellant's statement that he drove the truck was properly admitted when, prior to introducing it, appellee State established that more likely than not the crime of drunk driving had occurred. Finally, appellant waived his sentencing claim when a concise statement of why the sentence imposed compromised the sentencing scheme as a whole was not included in his appeal.


OUTCOME: Since appellant was charged with driving while intoxicated, evidence showing amount of alcohol in appellant's blood was more than 0.10 percent was properly admitted under statute. Sentencing claim was waived when no statement of why sentence imposed compromised sentencing scheme as a whole was included in appeal.

Commonwealth v. Moyer


No. 1947 WDA 2015, No. 1948 WDA 2015, No. 1949 WDA 2015


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2016 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 4708; 159 A.3d 999



December 9, 2016, Decided
